Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Building Proofs on Disputed Premises: Ilzami vs Tahqiqi
Methodological qawida on using disputed premises in fatwa arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ilzami and tahqiqi proofs and apply the qawida 'bina' al-mukhtalaf 'ala al-mukhtalaf fih' to evaluate when a disputed premise can be used in a fatwa.

Core Idea
A disputed premise cannot compel an opponent but can clarify the truth.

When constructing a fatwa, a mufti often needs to argue using premises that the opposing school might reject. The classical Hanafi maxim 'Building a disputed matter on a disputed premise' distinguishes between two types of proofs: ilzami (binding) and tahqiqi (investigative). This lesson unpacks that distinction through a concrete fiqh example involving two pilgrims in ihram who jointly kill game. Understanding this qawida protects you from misusing disputed evidence in inter-madhhab debates and sharpens your fatwa methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
The passage begins with a question: can a disputed premise (like the homonym argument) be used as proof against an opponent who does not accept it? Recognize that this is a methodological issue in usul al-iftā'.
The question arises from a previous discussion where the author preferred a proof that Shafi'is contest.
2
Distinguish Ilzami vs Tahqiqi
Extract the core distinction: ilzami proofs aim to bind the opponent and must rest on agreed premises; tahqiqi proofs aim to uncover truth and may use disputed premises. Note that tahqiqi does not intend to compel.
Ilzami is like forensic proof; tahqiqi is like academic research.
3
State the Qawida
Formulate the maxim: 'بناء المختلف على المختلف فيه لا يصح في الدليل الإلزامي، ويصح في الدليل التحقيقي' ('Basing a disputed matter on a disputed premise is invalid in ilzami proofs, valid in tahqiqi proofs').
This is a sughra (minor) maxim, also considered a dabt (restrictive rule).
4
Analyze the Fiqh Example
Examine the two muhrim case: Hanafis rule each pays a full penalty because each violated his own ihram (expiation view). Shafi'is rule one penalty because the penalty compensates the game (substitute view). The Hanafi proof relies on the premise that penalty is expiation—which Shafi'is reject. Yet Hanafis use it as a tahqiqi proof to explain their position, not to bind the opponent.
The illustration shows the practical application: the same premise is valid for clarification but not for coercion.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Note the practical consequence: in Hanafi fatwa, two penalties are given; in Shafi'i fatwa, one penalty. The qawida explains why Hanafi muftis can still articulate their reasoning even when Shafi'is disagree.
This confirms the maxim 'لا إنكار في مسائل الاجتهاد' (no denial in matters of ijtihad).

سوال: والثانی اوجہ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ لانہ مشترک کو بھی دلیل بنانا جائز ہے اگر چہ اول دلیل زیادہ بہتر ہے حالانکہ عموم مشترک شوافع کے مقابلہ میں دلیل نہیں بن سکتا کیونکہ وہ عموم مشترک کے قائل ہیں تو یہاں بناء المختلف علی المختلف فیہ لازم آ رہا ہے جو جائز نہیں ہے۔
جواب: مسئلہ مختلف کی بنیاد مختلف فیہ پر دلیل الزامی میں درست نہیں ہے البتہ دلیل تحقیقی میں مختلف فیہ کو مختلف فیہ کا مدار بنا کر کسی چیز کی وضاحت درست ہے اگر چہ اس طریقہ سے کسی چیز کو لازم کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ جس کی تفصیل اس مسئلہ سے معلوم ہو جاتی ہے کہ اگر دو محرم کسی شکار کے قتل میں شریک ہوئے تو ہمارے نزدیک دونوں پر پوری پوری جزاء واجب ہوگی اس لئے کہ ہر ایک نے اپنے احرام پر جنایت کا ارتکاب کیا ہے۔ کیا آپ کو معلوم نہیں کہ حالت احرام میں اگر کوئی شکار کی طرف رہنمائی کر دے تو اس رہنمائی کرنے والے پر بھی جزاء واجب ہے تو شرکت تو دلالت و رہنمائی سے بھی بڑھ کر ہے جب رہنمائی کرنے کی صورت میں جزاء واجب ہے تو شرکت میں بدرجہ اولی واجب ہوگی و عند الشافعی علیہما جزاء واحد اس اختلاف کا مدار ایک دوسرے اختلاف پر ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ جو جزاء شکار کی وجہ سے واجب ہوگی وہ صرف شکار کا بدل ہے اس میں امام شافعی کے نزدیک کفارہ کے معنی نہیں ہیں لہذا شکار کے واحد ہونے کی صورت میں جزا واحد ہے۔
Question: From 'and the second is more appropriate' it appears that using 'because it is a homonym' as a proof is permissible, even though the first proof is better, whereas the generality of homonyms cannot be used as proof against the Shafi'is because they are proponents of the generality of homonyms; thus building a disputed matter on another disputed matter becomes necessary, which is not permissible. Answer: Basing a disputed issue on another disputed issue is not correct in an obligatory (ilzami) proof, but in a research (tahqiqi) proof, making a disputed matter the basis of clarification of another disputed matter is correct, even though making something necessary by this method is not correct. The detail is understood from this issue: If two muhrim (pilgrims in ihram) jointly kill some game, then according to us (Hanafis) both are liable for a full penalty each, because each has committed an offense against his own ihram. Do you not know that if someone guides toward the game while in ihram, then that guide is also liable for a penalty? Then partnership (in the killing) is even more than guiding; when guiding incurs a penalty, then partnership incurs it a fortiori. According to al-Shafi'i, upon both is one penalty. The basis of this difference is another difference: the penalty that becomes obligatory due to the game is merely a substitute for the game; according to Imam al-Shafi'i it does not have the meaning of expiation, therefore in the case of a single game, the penalty is single.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage addresses a methodological rule in usul al-iftā': whether a disputed premise (مختلف فيه) can serve as evidence for another disputed issue. The question arises because the author previously considered the second proof (that 'hukm' is a homonym with no general meaning) as 'more appropriate' (اوجه), but this proof itself is disputed between Hanafis and Shafi'is. So the questioner asks: how can a disputed matter be used as evidence against an opponent who disputes it? The answer distinguishes between two types of proofs: ilzami proofs (الزامی, obligatory proofs meant to compel the opponent) and tahqiqi proofs (تحقیقی, proofs aimed at establishing the truth). In ilzami proofs, building on a disputed premise is invalid because the opponent does not accept the premise. However, in tahqiqi proofs, it is permissible to use a disputed premise to clarify a related issue, as long as it is not being imposed as a binding argument. The example given is the case of two muhrims jointly killing game. Hanafis hold each must pay a full penalty (جزاء) because each has violated ihram. Shafi'is hold only one penalty because they consider the penalty as simply a compensation for the game, not an expiation. The Hanafi argument uses the analogy of guidance (دلالت) to show that partnership is even more serious, but that analogy itself relies on a disputed point (whether the penalty is compensation or expiation). Thus, the Hanafi position is built on a premise that the Shafi'i does not accept. However, since it is a tahqiqi proof (not an ilzami attempt to bind the Shafi'i), it is permissible. This demonstrates the qawida: 'Building a disputed issue on another disputed issue is not allowed in ilzami proofs, but is allowed in tahqiqi proofs.'

Key Terms
دلیل الزامی (dalil ilzami): A proof used to compel the opponent, which must be based on premises accepted by the opponent.
دلیل تحقیقی (dalil tahqiqi): A proof aimed at investigating and clarifying the truth, even if based on disputed premises.
جزاء (jaza'): Penalty, expiation, or compensation, often for hunting violations in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qawida in this lesson, in which type of proof is it permissible to build a disputed issue on a disputed premise?
A) Ilzami proof
B) Tahqiqi proof
C) Both ilzami and tahqiqi
D) Neither ilzami nor tahqiqi

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti may use a disputed premise as a tahqiqi proof to explain his position, but not as an ilzami proof to compel opponents.

Interpreting 'Hukm' in the Hadith of Intentions as Otherworldly
Defends otherworldly interpretation of 'hukm'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a solitary hadith (khabar wahid) cannot establish wujub, and evaluate the arguments for interpreting 'hukm' in the hadith of intentions as otherworldly.

Core Idea
The hadith of intentions governs otherworldly reward, not worldly validity—a solitary report cannot impose obligation.

In this passage, the commentator defends the interpretation that the implied word 'hukm' in the famous hadith 'innamal a'malu binniyyah' refers to otherworldly reward and punishment, not to the worldly validity of acts. He addresses objections to this view using usul principles about consensus, homonymy, and the limitation of khabar wahid. This discussion is essential for muftis who must correctly apply the hadith without overstepping its legal force.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
State that the author interprets the implied word 'hukm' as otherworldly reward/punishment (thawab/iqab), not worldly validity (sihhat/fasad).
The hadith is treated as having an implied (muqaddar) word 'hukm'.
2
Examine the first proof: consensus
The first proof is the consensus on 'la thawaba wa la iqaba illa binniyyah'. Note the objection that this consensus does not preclude worldly meaning because reward depends on validity.
The author replies that worldly and otherworldly hukm are not equivalent; a valid act may lack reward.
3
Analyze the second proof: homonymy
The second proof argues that 'hukm' is a homonym (mushtarak) and thus cannot be taken generally. The objector distinguishes verbal vs. semantic homonyms; Hanafis accept generality for semantic homonyms.
The reply is that the objection fails because the two meanings are not used with equal frequency.
4
Evaluate the third proof: preventing naskh
The third proof from al-Mustasfa states that taking worldly meaning would necessitate abrogation (naskh) of the Qur'an's absolute command on wudu by a solitary hadith, which is impermissible.
Also, the Prophet taught wudu to the Bedouin without mentioning intention.
5
Understand the final response to Qasim ibn Qutlubugha
Qasim's alternative (interpreting 'a'mal' as acts of worship) would wrongly establish wujub of intention from a khabar wahid. Hence the otherworldly interpretation is the only valid one.
A khabar wahid can only establish sunnah or mustahabb, not obligation.

ماقبل میں صاحب کتاب نے حدیث میں انما الاعمال بالنیات میں بطور اقتضاء حکم مقدر مان کر حکم سے حکم اخروی مراد لیا اور اس پر تین دلیلیں قائم کی ہیں۔ ہر دلیل پر اعتراض ہے ذیل میں ان اعتراضات اور جوابات کو نقل کیا جا رہا ہے۔

اجتماعی ہے اس لئے حکم دنیوی مراد نہیں ہو سکتا ۔ (1) پہلی دلیل تھی کہ لا ثواب ولا عقاب الا بالنية اجماعی مسئلہ ہے اور اس میں حکم سے حکم اخروی بھی

معترض کہتا ہے کہ محکم اخروی اجتماعی مسئلہ ہے لا نواب ولا عقاب الا بالنية میں یہ بات تو تسلیم ہے لیکن یہ اجتماع فریق مخالف کے دعوی کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے تو مانع اور رکاوٹ نہیں ہے اس طور پر کہ حکم سے حکم دنیوی مراد لیا جائے اور جب صحت و فساد ہی کا مدار نیت پر ہوگا تو ثواب و عقاب کا مدار تو بدرجہ اولی نیست پر ہوگا کیونکہ ثواب عقاب کا ترتب تو صحت و فساد پر ہی ہوتا ہے۔ دوسری دلیل تھی کہ لفظ حکم مشترک ہے اور مشترک میں عموم نہیں ہوتا اس پر اعتراض یہ ہے کہ مشترک کی دو قسمیں ہیں: (۱) لفظی (۲) معنوی ،مشترک لفظی میں عموم نہیں ہوتا لیکن مشترک معنوی میں تو احناف بھی عموم کے قائل ہیں جیسے شئی اور اس پر مرتب ہونے والے اثر کو حکم کہتے ہیں اور یہ بھی مشترک معنوی ہوا۔

جواب: یہ اعتراض اس وقت صحیح قرار دیا جا سکتا ہے جب لفظ حکم دنیوی اور اخروی دونوں پر بطور تساوی بولا جائے حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے، کیونکہ حکم دنیوی اگر چہ اعمال پر مرتب ہونے والے اثر کا نام ہے لیکن حکم اخروی صحیح مذہب کے مطابق ایسا نہیں ہے کیونکہ بسا اوقات عمل صحیح ہوتا ہے اور اس پر ثواب مرتب نہیں ہوتا اور عمل فاسد ہوتا ہے لیکن اس پر عقاب مرتب نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اللہ تعالیٰ معاف کر دیتا ہے۔
اس پر دوسرا اعتراض یہ ہے کہ جیسے آپ نے کہا کہ ہم نے حکم اخروی مراد لیا ہے اور چونکہ یہ مشترک لفظی ہے لہذا حکم دنیوی مراد لینے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے تو اس کو اسطرح بھی کہہ سکتے ہیں کہ مشترک لفظی ہے لہذا ہم نے حکم دنیوی مراد لے لیا تو اب حکم اخروی مراد لینے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور اس صورت میں الاعمال سے مراد عبادات مقصودہ ہونگی۔ چونکہ ادلہ ثلاثہ پر اعتراض ہوتے ہیں اس لئے حکم اخروی کی تعیین اور اس پر اجماع کا دعوی ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔
اسی لئے صاحب مستصفی نے دلیل اجتماع میں دوسرا اسلوب اپنایا ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں بطور اقتضاء حکم دنیوی مراد لینے کی صورت میں خبر واحد سے کتاب اللہ کا نسخ لازم آتا ہے، حالانکہ سخ کتاب اللہ بخبر الواحد جائز نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ اللہ تعالی نے کتاب اللہ میں اعضاء وضو کو مطلقاً دھونے کا حکم صادر فرمایا ، حدیث مذکورہ میں حکم دنیوی مراد لینے کی صورت میں اس مطلق حکم کا مقید کرنا لازم آئیگا نیز نبی اکرم صلی اللہ علی وسلم نے اعرابی کو وضوء کی تعلیم دی اور نیت کو ذکر نہیں کیا اگر نیت اعمال کے جواز اور ان کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے شرط ہوتی تو آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اس کو ضرور ذکر کرتے اس تفصیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ حدیث " انــمــا الاعـمـال بالنیات میں لفظ محذوف حکم سے حکم اخروی ہی مراد ہے۔

اعتراض : علامہ قاسم ابن قطلوبغا نے حدیث کا جو مطلب بیان کیا ہے وہ زیادہ بہتر ہے اس سے کہ حدیث میں بطور اقتضاء حکم سے حکم اخروی مراد لیا جائے کیونکہ اس میں سراسر تکلفات ہیں انہوں نے کہا انما الاعمال بالنيات میں الاعمال سے اعمال مخصوصہ یعنی عبادات مقصودہ مراد لئے جائیں اور عبادت مقصودہ صحیح ہونے کے لئے نیت ضروری اور واجب ہے اس سے کلام بھی درست ہو جائیگا اور یہ مسئلہ متفق علیہ بھی ہے۔ جواب: اگر یوں کہا جائے کہ حدیث میں الاعمال سے مراد عبادات مقصودہ ہیں یا حکم مقدر مان کر اس سے حکم دنیوی مراد لیا جائے تو اس حدیث سے نیت کے وجوب کو ثابت کرنا لازم آتا ہے حالانکہ یہ حدیث ظنی الثبوت اور ظنی الہ ہے اور حدیث ظنی الثبوت اور ظنی الدلالہ سے کسی چیز کے وجوب کو ثابت نہیں کیا جاتا، زیادہ سے زیادہ اس طرح کی خبر واحد سے سنیت و استحباب کو ثابت کیا جا سکتا ہے، اسلئے حکم کو مقدر مان کر حکم اخروی مراد لینے پر اجماع ہو گیا اور جب حکم اخروی مراد ہو گیا تو چونکہ حکم مشترک ہے اس لئے اب دوسرے معنی یعنی حکم دنیوی مراد نہیں ہو سکتے ۔ صاحب کتاب نے ثواب کو مطلقاً اور عقاب کو لفظ استحقاق کے ساتھ ذکر کر کے ایک خاص نکتہ کی طرف اشارہ فرمایا ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ جب بندہ نیک عمل کرتا ہے تو اللہ تعالی ضرور اس پر اجر وثواب کرتا ہے اور جب کوئی گناہ کرتا
الدلالة
Previously the author (sahib al-kitab) took the hadith 'innamal a'malu bin niyyat' with an implied (muqaddar) word 'hukm', and intended by 'hukm' the otherworldly reward/punishment, and established three proofs for it. Objections are raised against each proof; below those objections and answers are being transmitted. It is agreed that worldly hukm cannot be intended. (1) The first proof was that 'la thawaba wa la iqaba illa binniyyah' is a matter of consensus, and in it 'hukm' means otherworldly. The objector says: The otherworldly judgement is a matter of consensus; in 'la thawaba wa la iqaba illa binniyyah' this is accepted, but this consensus does not preclude the opponent's claim that 'hukm' means worldly, because when validity/invalidity depends on intention, then reward/punishment depends on it a fortiori, since reward and punishment follow upon validity/invalidity. The second proof was that the word 'hukm' is homonymous (mushtarak) and a homonym does not have generality. Objection: Mushtarak is of two types: (1) lafdhi (verbal homonym) and (2) ma'nawi (semantic homonym). A verbal homonym has no generality, but Hanafis do hold that semantic homonyms have generality—like 'shay' (thing) and the effect that follows upon it is called 'hukm'. This is also a semantic homonym. Answer: This objection would be valid if the word 'hukm' were used equally for both worldly and otherworldly, but it is not. Because worldly hukm is the name of the effect that follows upon actions, but otherworldly hukm, according to the correct school, is not like that; because sometimes an action is valid but no reward follows, and sometimes an action is invalid but no punishment follows—rather Allah forgives. A second objection: Just as you said that we intended otherworldly hukm, and since it is a verbal homonym, there is no need to intend worldly hukm, so too we could say that because it is a verbal homonym, we intend worldly hukm, and then there is no need for otherworldly hukm; in that case 'a'mal' would mean specific acts of worship. Because the three proofs are objectionable, the determination of otherworldly hukm and the claim of consensus are not established. For this reason, the author of al-Mustasfa adopted a different approach in the collective proof. Its gist is that if one takes 'hukm' in the hadith as intended by implication (taqdir) to mean worldly, then it would necessitate abrogation (naskh) of the Book of Allah by a solitary report (khabar wahid), which is not permissible because Allah in His Book commanded the washing of the limbs of wudu absolutely; taking worldly hukm would necessitate restricting that absolute command. Also, the Prophet taught wudu to the Bedouin without mentioning intention; if intention were a condition for validity, he would have mentioned it. From this detail it is known that in the hadith 'innamal a'malu binniyyah', the implied word 'hukm' means otherworldly. Objection: Allamah Qasim ibn Qutlubugha said that the meaning he gave is better than taking 'hukm' as otherworldly by implication, because that involves unnecessary complications. He said to take 'a'mal' in 'innamal a'malu binniyyah' as specific acts (i.e., acts of worship) and for an act of worship to be valid, intention is necessary and obligatory; the speech becomes correct and this is agreed upon. Answer: If it is said that 'a'mal' in the hadith means specific acts of worship, or by taking an implied 'hukm' one intends worldly, then it would necessitate establishing the obligation (wujub) of intention from this hadith, whereas this hadith is speculative in its transmission and speculative in its indication, and a hadith that is speculative in transmission and indication cannot establish the obligation of anything; at most, such a solitary report can establish sunnah and mustahabb. Therefore, there is consensus on taking 'hukm' as implied and intending otherworldly. And when otherworldly is intended, since 'hukm' is a homonym, the other meaning (worldly) cannot be intended. The author (sahib al-kitab) mentioned 'thawab' absolutely and 'iqab' with the word 'istihqaq' to indicate a special point, namely that when a servant does a good deed, Allah certainly gives him reward; and when he commits a sin...
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul discussion on interpreting the hadith 'innamal a'malu binniyyat'. The author (commentator) explains that the original matn's author took the hadith with an implied word 'hukm' and interpreted it as otherworldly reward/punishment, not worldly validity. Three proofs are given, each with objections and responses. The first proof: 'la thawaba wa la iqaba illa binniyyah' is consensus that intention determines otherworldly outcome. Objector: that consensus does not prevent worldly interpretation. Response: worldly hukm and otherworldly hukm are not equivalent; sometimes a valid act has no reward. Second proof: 'hukm' is a homonym, so it cannot be taken generally. Objector: only verbal homonyms lack generality; semantic homonyms (like 'shay') can be general. Response: the objection would stand if both meanings were equal, but they are not. Third proof: if worldly hukm were intended, a solitary hadith would abrogate the Qur'an (e.g., wudu verses). Objection from Qasim ibn Qutlubugha: better to interpret 'a'mal' as acts of worship. Response: that would make intention obligatory (wajib), but the hadith is speculative and cannot establish obligation. Therefore, the only valid interpretation is that 'hukm' refers to otherworldly reward/punishment. This is a rasm al-mufti principle: how to weigh conflicting interpretations of a text.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): A homonymous term that can mean worldly legal effect (sihhat/fasad) or otherworldly reward/punishment (thawab/iqab).
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A solitary hadith that is not mutawatir; it is speculative in transmission (dhanni al-thubut) and cannot abrogate the Qur'an or establish obligation.
اقتضاء (iqtida'): Implied meaning; here, 'hukm' is not explicitly stated but is implied in the hadith (muqaddar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why can't the hadith 'innamal a'malu binniyyah' be interpreted as establishing the obligation (wujub) of intention for worldly validity?
A) Because it is a mutawatir hadith.
B) Because it is a solitary hadith with speculative transmission and indication.
C) Because the Qur'an explicitly abrogates it.
D) Because it applies only to prayers.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of intentions governs otherworldly reward; a solitary report cannot impose obligation for worldly validity.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

Intention in Washing the Deceased: Obligation vs. Purity
Explains the distinction between niyyah for purity and for obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when intention (niyyah) is required in ghusl al-mayyit and apply the rule to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Intention is needed to lift the communal obligation, not to achieve physical purity.

When washing a deceased person, many assume intention is always necessary. However, Hanafi fiqh separates two effects: physical purification and discharging the communal duty. This lesson, drawn from the Ashbah wa al-Nazair tradition, clarifies that intention is tied to obligation, not purity—a key distinction for the mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects
Recognize that ghusl al-mayyit has a dual nature: (1) attaining physical purity for the corpse, and (2) lifting the fard kifayah from the community.
2
Understand the role of intention
According to the text, intention (niyyah) is not a condition for the act itself achieving purity; it is only required to remove the obligation from the responsible persons.
3
Apply to the drowning case
If a person drowns, the water purifies the body. Thus, the first aspect is automatically fulfilled. The remaining need for washing is solely to discharge the obligation—hence intention becomes critical.
4
Recognize the rasm al-mufti principle
This case illustrates a methodological rule: the mufti must determine where intention is integral (for obligation) and where it is not (for inherent purity).

کفایہ کو اپنے اوپر سے ساقط کرنے کے لئے نیت کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ فرض کفایہ ادا ہو جائے تو ہم نے حصول طہارت اور میت پر نماز جنازہ کے بیچ ہونے کے لئے نیت کو شرط قرار نہیں دیا ہے بلکہ مظلفین کے ذمہ سے فرض کو ساقط کرنے کیلئے ہم نے نیت کو ضروری قرار دیا ہے دونوں کے فرق کو سمجھ لیجئے۔ بقول علامہ حموی عسل دینے والے ہی کا نیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ بوقت غسل مکلفین میں سے کوئی بھی نیت کرلے سب کی طرف سے کافی ہے۔
اسی پر صاحب کتاب ایک تفریح پیش کرتے ہیں: کہ اگر کوئی شخص تالاب میں ڈوب کر مر جائے تو تالاب میں ڈوب کر مرنے سے میت پاک ہو جائیگی لیکن مکلفین کے ذمہ سے فرض کو ساقط کرنے کے لئے غریق کو غسل دینا ضروری ہے۔ غسل میت میں دو چیزیں ہیں: (۱) حصول طہارت (۲) مکلفین کے ذمہ سے فرض کو ساقط کرنا۔ ڈوب کر مرنے سے طہارت میت تو حاصل ہو جائیگی اور اس پر نماز جنازہ بھی پڑھنا درست ہوگا لیکن دوسری چیز ہے مکلفین کے ذمہ سے فرض کا ساقط ہونا اول میں نیت ضروری نہیں ہے دوسرے میں نیت کرنا ضروری ہے۔ پانی میں ڈوب کر مرنے والے کی میت کو غسل دینے کی تین صورتیں ہیں:
(1) میت کو تین مرتبہ غسل دینا ضروری ہے سی امام ابی یوسف کا قول ہے۔ (۲) امام محمد کے نزدیک اگر میت کو پانی سے نکالتے وقت غسل کی نیت کی ہے تو دومرتبہ نسل دینا ضروری ہے اور نیت نہ کرنے کی صورت میں تین مرتبہ مسل دینا ضروری ہے۔ (۳) امام صاحب کے نزدیک ایک مرتبہ غسل دیا جائیگا یہی ایک روایت امام محمد کی ہے جیسا کہ فتح القدیر میں اسکی تفصیل موجود ہے۔
Intention is necessary to remove the obligation from oneself so that the communal obligation is fulfilled. We have not stipulated intention for attaining purity and for the funeral prayer over the deceased; rather, we have made intention necessary to remove the obligation from the shoulders of those responsible. Understand the difference between the two. According to Allamah Hamawi, intention by the one actually washing is not necessary; rather, any of those responsible may make intention at the time of washing, and it suffices for all. The author also presents an application: if a person drowns in a pond, the corpse becomes pure by drowning, but to remove the obligation from the responsible, washing the drowned person is necessary. Washing the deceased has two aspects: (1) attaining purity, and (2) removing the obligation from the responsible. By drowning, purity is attained, and funeral prayer upon it is valid, but the second aspect—removal of the obligation—requires intention; the first does not require intention, the second does. There are three scenarios for washing the drowned: (1) According to Imam Abu Yusuf, it is necessary to wash three times. (2) According to Imam Muhammad, if at the time of removal from water one had intention for washing, two washes suffice; without intention, three are required. (3) According to Imam Abu Hanifa, one wash suffices; this is also one narration from Imam Muhammad, as detailed in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage clarifies the role of intention (niyyah) in the ritual washing of the deceased (ghusl al-mayyit). The author distinguishes two separate legal effects: achieving physical purity for the corpse (which does not require intention) and lifting the communal obligation (fard kifaya) from the Muslim community (which does require intention). He then applies this to a drowning case: the water naturally purifies the body, so the obligation of washing for purity is satisfied; however, the obligation on the living to perform the washing is not fulfilled unless a person makes intention at the time of washing. The passage also presents the three positions of the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) on the number of washes required for a drowned person when intention is made or not. This is a rasm rule (methodological rule) because it establishes a general principle about when intention is obligatory in communal obligations.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention; a mental determination to perform an act for the sake of Allah, required for removing obligation but not for physical purity.
فرض کفایہ (fard kifayah): Communal obligation; sufficient if some perform it; intention needed to lift obligation from oneself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary purpose of intention (niyyah) in washing a deceased person?
A) To make the washing legally valid as a purification act.
B) To remove the communal obligation from the community.
C) To ensure the body becomes physically clean.
D) To allow the funeral prayer to be offered.

Key Takeaway
Intention in ghusl al-mayyit is for discharging the fard kifayah, not for achieving purification.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Number of Washes for a Drowned Person
Presents the three Hanafi positions on washing a drowned person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on washing a drowned person and evaluate their practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
The number of washes for a drowned person varies by imam: Abu Hanifa says one, Abu Yusuf says three, Muhammad splits based on intention.

While the general rule about intention is settled, the imams differed on its specific application when washing a drowned person. Their views produce different outcomes depending on the presence or absence of intention at the time of removal from water. This lesson unpacks each position and its practical effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three imams' positions
List what each of the three major Hanafi imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—says about the number of washes for a drowned person.
2
Link intention to the numbers
Note that Muhammad's position explicitly ties the number of washes to intention: two if intention is made at removal, three if not. Abu Yusuf always requires three; Abu Hanifa always one.
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: the number of required washes differs based on whose view is followed, affecting how the community carries out the washing.
4
Recognize the lack of tarjih in the text
The passage presents the dispute without preferring one view, referring to Fath al-Qadir for details. This is typical of later texts that record ikhtilaf without settling it.

Intention is necessary to remove the obligation from oneself so that the communal obligation is fulfilled. We have not stipulated intention for attaining purity and for the funeral prayer over the deceased; rather, we have made intention necessary to remove the obligation from the shoulders of those responsible. Understand the difference between the two. According to Allamah Hamawi, intention by the one actually washing is not necessary; rather, any of those responsible may make intention at the time of washing, and it suffices for all. The author also presents an application: if a person drowns in a pond, the corpse becomes pure by drowning, but to remove the obligation from the responsible, washing the drowned person is necessary. By drowning, purity is attained, and funeral prayer upon it is valid, but the second aspect—removal of the obligation—requires intention; the first does not require intention, the second does. There are three scenarios for washing the drowned: (1) According to Imam Abu Yusuf, it is necessary to wash three times. (2) According to Imam Muhammad, if at the time of removal from water one had intention for washing, two washes suffice; without intention, three are required. (3) According to Imam Abu Hanifa, one wash suffices; this is also one narration from Imam Muhammad, as detailed in Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
غریق (ghariq): A person who drowns; in this context, a drowned corpse that is already purified by water.
تفریع (tafri‘): A practical application or derivation from a general rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many washes are required if a drowned person is removed from water and the washer makes intention at that time, according to Imam Muhammad?
A) One wash.
B) Two washes.
C) Three washes.
D) None, since the body is already pure.

Key Takeaway
The number of washes for a drowned person varies among the Hanafi imams, showing the flexibility within the school.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

Intention in Acts of Worship: The Exception of Islam
Explains rule: intention required in all worship except entering Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that intention is not required for worldly Islam and distinguish between the conditions for validity of Islam and disbelief in fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Worldly Islam is valid by mere declaration; intention is only required for acts of worship, not for entering Islam.

This lesson addresses a fundamental rasm al-mufti rule: intention (niyyah) is a condition for the validity of all acts of worship except the act of becoming Muslim (Islam). As a mufti, you must know when intention is required and when it is not, especially in cases of coercion (ikrah). The passage also distinguishes between worldly Islam (dunyawi) and otherworldly Islam (ukhrawi), which has direct implications for issuing fatwas on apostasy and conversion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its scope
Find the general rule: intention is a condition for validity of all acts of worship (al-‘ibādāt al-maqṣūdah). Then note the exception: Islam is valid without intention.
The rule is from the matn of al-Ashbah wa al-Nazā’ir.
2
Understand the exception: Islam
Examine why intention is not required for Islam. The evidence is the case of the coerced person (mukrah): his verbal declaration of Islam is valid even though he may not have intended it. This proves that outward submission suffices for worldly purposes.
The hadith of Usāmah (r.a.) supports this: the Prophet ﷺ did not require splitting the heart to check intention.
3
Distinguish worldly vs. otherworldly Islam
Worldly Islam (dunyawi) is established by mere verbal declaration, leading to application of Islamic laws (inheritance, burial, etc.). Otherworldly Islam (ukhrawi) requires inward faith (īmān) and intention. This distinction is crucial for a mufti when assessing a person’s status.
The passage states: 'Inward submission is called īmān, outward submission is called Islām.'
4
Apply the rule to coercion
If a person is coerced into declaring Islam, his Islam is valid for worldly matters. He cannot be killed, nor can it be said that he accepted Islam insincerely. This ruling is based on the principle that intention is not a condition for the validity of Islam.
Contrast with coercion into disbelief (kufr): intention is required for kufr, as disbelief is an abandonment (tark) and intention suffices for abandonment.
5
Contrast with disbelief (kufr)
Unlike Islam, becoming a disbeliever requires intention. Committing acts of disbelief without intending kufr does not make one a kafir. This is because disbelief is defined as abandonment (tark) and intention is sufficient for abandoning acts.
The passage emphasizes that intention is a condition for kufr but not for Islam, a unique Hanafi position.

وَأَمَّا فِي الْعِبَادَاتِ كُلَّهَا فَهِيَ شَرْطُ صِحْتِهَا إِلَّا الْإِسْلَامُ فَإِنَّهُ يَصِحُ بِدُونِهَا بِدَلِيْلٍ قَوْلِهِمْ إِنَّ إسْلَامَ الْمُكْرَهِ صَحِيْحٌ وَلَا يَكُونُ مُسْلِماً بِمُجَرَّدِ نِيَّةِ الْإِسْلَامِ بِخِلَافِ الْكُفْرِ كَمَا سنبيلة فِي بَحْث التروي.
ترجمہ: اور بہر حال تمام عبادات میں سوائے اسلام کے نیت عبادات کی صحت کی شرط ہے کیونکہ اسلام بدون نیت صحیح ہو جاتا ہے دلیل فقہاء کا یہ ارشاد ہے کہ مرہ کا اسلام درست ہے اور محض اسلام کی نیت سے مسلمان نہیں ہوگا بخلاف کفر کے اس کو ہم تروک کی بحث میں بیان کریں گے۔ تشریح: مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ جملہ عبادات مقصودہ کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے نیت کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے عبادات مقصودہ کی تعریف ماقبل میں کی جاچکی ہے، البتہ صحت اسلام کے لئے نیت ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ اسلام کے معتبر ہونے کے لئے صرف اظہار اسلام کافی ہے لیکن یہ بات ذہن میں رہے کہ اسلام کی دو حیثیتیں ہیں (۱) دنیوی (۲) اخروی۔
دنیوی اسلام مطلب یہ ہے کہ دنیا کے اندر اسلامی حکومت یا اسلامی معاشرہ میں رہنے والا محض زبان سے اظہار ا سلام کر دے تو اس پر اسلامی احکام جاری ہو نگے لہذا اسے اپنے وارثین کی میراث بھی ملے گی اور مسلمانوں کے قبرستان میں فین بھی ہو گا اس حیثیت سے اظہار اسلام کافی ہے، البتہ اخروی اعتبار سے کہ اس کے ساتھ آخرت میں وہی اعزاز و اکرام کیا جائے گا جو مسلمانوں کے ساتھ کیا جائیگا تو اس کے لئے زبان و قلب سے ایمان لانا ضروری ہے محض اسلام کا اظہار کافی نہیں ہوگا۔
انقیاد باطنی کو ایمان کہتے ہیں اور انقیا د ظاہری کو اسلام کہتے ہیں۔
بصح دنیوی اسلام کے معتبر ہونے کے لئے محض اظہار اسلام کافی ہے نیت ضروری نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے کسی پر زبر دستی کی اور کہا کہ اسلام قبول کر لے ورنہ جان سے مارڈالونگا اور وہ مکر و زبان سے اظہار اسلام کر دے تو اس کے اسلام کا اعتبار ہوگا اور اسکوقتل کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا اور یہ نہیں کہا جائیگا جان بچانے کی خاطر اس نے اسلام قبول کیا ہے۔ جس کی تائید ایک حدیث سے ہوتی ہے جس میں حضرت اسامہ نے اظہار اسلام کے بعد بھی ایک آدمی کا قتل کر دیا تھا اور جب پورا واقعہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے سامنے پیش کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا ” افلا شققت عن قلبه حتى تعلم اقالها ام لا‘ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اسلام کے معتبر ہونے کیلئے اظہار اسلام کافی ہے نیت ضروری نہیں۔
ولا يكون مسلما لا یکون کی ضمیر میں دو احتمال ہیں (۱) مکرہ (۲) کافر۔ اول صورت : میں مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی پر زبردستی کی گئی اور اس نے اسلام کی نیت کر لی زبان سے کلمہ شہادتین کا تلفظ نہ کیا تو اس کا اسلام معتبر نہ ہوگا اور وہ مسلمان شمار نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اسلام اوامر و نواہی کا نام ہے اور یہ افعال صرف نیت سے ادا نہیں ہوں گے بلکہ ان کیلئے فعل کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے۔
دوسری صورت : جب یکون کی ضمیر کا مرجع کا فر ہو جیسا کہ سیاق وسباق سے سمجھا جا سکتا ہے اس صورت میں مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ اگر کوئی کا فر صرف اسلام کی نیت کرلے اور زبان سے کلمہ شہادتین کا تلفظ نہ کرے تو دنیوی اعتبار ہے اس کا اسلام معتبر نہ ہوگا ، اخروی اعتبار سے مسلمان ہوگا یا نہیں یہ تو صرف اللہ ہی جانتا ہے۔ بخلاف کفر کے اگر کوئی م کفر کی نیت کر لے تو وہ کا فر ہو جائے گا کیونکہ کفر کسی چیز کو چھوڑنے اور ترک کا نام ہے اور ترک فعل میں نیت کافی ہے جیسا کہ اسکی تفصیل آرہی ہے ۔ واما الكفر الخ: اگر کوئی شخص اعمال کفریہ کا ارتکاب کرے لیکن اسکی نیت کفر کی نہ ہو تو محض اعمال کفریہ کرنے سے وہ شخص کافر نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اسلام کے معتبر ہونے کیلئے اظہار اسلام شرط ہے اسی طرح کافر ہونے کے لئے بھی نیت شرط ہے۔ دلیل : اس کی یہ ہے کہ فقہاء نے تصریح کی ہے کہ اگر کسی مسلمان پر جبر و اکراہ کر کے کلمات کفر سیا سکی زبان سے
And as for all acts of worship, intention is a condition for their validity, except Islam, for it is valid without intention, evidenced by their statement that the Islam of a coerced person is valid, and one does not become a Muslim merely by intending Islam, unlike disbelief, as we will mention in the discussion of al-tarawī. Translation: In all acts of worship, intention is a condition for their validity except Islam, because Islam becomes valid without intention. The evidence is the jurists' statement that the Islam of a coerced person is valid. One does not become Muslim merely by intending Islam, unlike disbelief, which we will explain in the discussion of al-tarawī. Explanation: The author states that intention is necessary for all intended acts of worship (al-‘ibādāt al-maqṣūdah) to be valid; this was defined previously. However, for the validity of Islam, intention is not necessary; rather, for Islam to be considered, mere verbal declaration suffices. But keep in mind that Islam has two aspects: (1) worldly and (2) otherworldly. Worldly Islam means that in an Islamic state or society, if a person merely verbalizes Islam, Islamic rulings apply to him; thus he inherits from his relatives and is buried in Muslim cemeteries. In this respect, mere declaration suffices. However, in the otherworldly aspect, that he be honored in the Hereafter as Muslims are, it is necessary to believe with heart and tongue; mere verbal declaration is not enough. Inward submission is called īmān, and outward submission is called Islām. For the validity of worldly Islam, mere declaration suffices; intention is not required. The evidence is that if someone is coerced and told to accept Islam or be killed, and he verbally declares Islam, his Islam is considered, and it is not permissible to kill him, nor is it said that he accepted Islam to save his life. This is supported by a hadith where Usama killed a man after he declared Islam, and when the incident was presented to the Prophet ﷺ, he said: 'Did you not split his heart to know whether he said it sincerely or not?' This hadith shows that for Islam to be considered, verbal declaration is sufficient; intention is not required. 'And he will not be Muslim' – the pronoun in 'lā yakūnu' has two possibilities: (1) the coerced person, (2) the disbeliever. In the first case: if someone is coerced and makes intention of Islam but does not utter the Shahada verbally, his Islam is not considered and he is not counted as Muslim, because Islam is defined by commands and prohibitions, and these actions cannot be performed by intention alone but require actual performance. In the second case, when the pronoun refers to the disbeliever, as can be understood from context, the meaning is that if a disbeliever merely intends Islam but does not verbally utter the Shahada, his Islam is not considered in worldly terms; as for the Hereafter, only Allah knows. Contrary to disbelief: if someone intends disbelief, he becomes a disbeliever, because disbelief is defined as abandoning and leaving, and in leaving, intention suffices, as will be detailed later. And as for disbelief: if a person commits acts of disbelief but does not intend disbelief, he does not become a disbeliever merely by committing those acts, because for Islam to be considered, verbal declaration is a condition; similarly, for disbelief, intention is a condition. The evidence is that jurists have explicitly stated that if a Muslim is compelled to utter words of disbelief under coercion, ...
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage establishes a foundational rasm rule: intention is a condition for the validity of all acts of worship except the act of entering Islam. The author explains the exception: becoming Muslim (entry into Islam) is valid without intention; mere verbal declaration (pronouncing the Shahada) is sufficient for worldly purposes. The evidence is the example of a coerced person (mukrah): if someone is forced to declare Islam under threat of death, his Islam is valid and he cannot be killed. This is supported by the hadith of Usama. The passage then clarifies that intention alone without verbal declaration does not make one a Muslim. The Hanafi school distinguishes between worldly Islam (which is valid by external submission) and otherworldly Islam (which requires inner faith). The passage also discusses the opposite: becoming a disbeliever (kufr) requires intention; committing sinful acts without intending disbelief does not render one a kafir. This is a crucial ruling for the mufti to know when issuing fatwas on apostasy.

Key Terms
اسلام (Islām): Outward submission by verbal declaration; valid even without intention for worldly purposes.
نیت (niyyah): Intention; required for validity of all acts of worship except Islam; required for kufr (disbelief) but not for Islam.
مکرہ (mukrah): One who is coerced or compelled; his declaration of Islam by force is valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Intention in the heart alone
B) Verbal declaration of the Shahada
C) Both intention and declaration
D) Performing Islamic duties for a period

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, entering Islam is the only act of worship that is valid without intention; mere verbal declaration establishes worldly Islam.

The Qada'/Diyanah Distinction in Oath Cases: Swearing Not to Lead Prayer
Ruling on oath-breaking with qada'/diyanah distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qada' (judicial) and diyanah (conscience) distinction to determine whether an imam who swore not to lead prayer is considered a breaker of his oath.

Core Idea
In oaths, the external act triggers judicial liability, but inner intention determines sin before Allah.

This passage from Al-Khaniyah illustrates a critical principle for muftis: the distinction between qada' and diyanah. When an imam swears not to lead prayer, but someone follows him, the ruling depends on whether we judge by apparent action or inner intent. The follower's prayer is valid, but the imam's liability breaks differently in court versus conscience.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
A man swears he will not lead anyone in prayer. Later, while he is praying alone, another person joins behind him with the intention of following. Determine whether the follower's prayer is valid and whether the imam breaks his oath.
2
Distinguish between Qada' and Diyanah
Understand that qada' is a judicial ruling based on external evidence (apparent actions), while diyanah considers inner intention and conscience. In this case, the imam did not intend to lead, so in diyanah he is not a breaker. However, because the act of following makes him appear as an imam, in qada' he is considered a breaker.
The Hanafi school holds that intentions are hidden and rulings are based on what is manifest.
3
Apply the Exception: Prior Witnesses
If before starting the prayer, the imam had witnesses testify that he is praying alone and not leading anyone, then even in qada' he is not considered a breaker. This exception highlights the importance of evidence in judicial rulings.
Witnesses make the hidden intention externally known.
4
Extend to Jumu'ah Prayer
The same rule applies if the oath-swearer leads Jumu'ah prayer: the prayer is valid, and he becomes hanith in qada'. This shows the rule is consistent across different prayer types.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if he swore that he would not lead anyone, and a person followed him, the following is valid. And does he become sinful (hanith)? It is said in al-Khaniyah: He becomes sinful in judgment (qada') but not in conscience (diyanah), except if he had witnesses before starting, then he does not become sinful in judgment. Likewise, if this one who swore led people in Jumu'ah prayer, it is valid and he becomes sinful in judgment. Translation: If someone swore that he will not lead anyone, and a person followed him, the following is valid. And will he be a breaker of oath? Al-Khaniyah said: He will be a breaker in judgment, not in conscience. But if he had witnesses before starting, then he will not be a breaker even in judgment. And similarly, if this oath-swearer led people in Jumu'ah prayer, the leading is valid and he becomes a breaker in judgment. Explanation: If someone swore not to lead, then one day he was praying alone, and someone came and joined with intention of following, his following is valid and the imamah also became valid. Because for following, intention to follow is necessary, but for the imam, intention of imamah is not a condition. In this case, due to the validity of imamah, the imam became a breaker and owes expiation for the oath. But this ruling is in judgment (qada'), not in conscience (diyanah). It will not be in conscience because due to not intending imamah, it cannot be said that he led, so he did not violate the oath, and he is not a breaker. And when people followed him, externally he became imam, but intention is hidden, and ruling is not attached to hidden matters. Therefore, in judgment he becomes a breaker. If before starting prayer he had witnesses that he is praying alone and not leading anyone, and then someone ...
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where a man swears that he will not lead anyone in prayer, but then someone comes and prays behind him. The ruling: the follower's prayer is valid (since he intended to follow), and the imam becomes a violator of his oath in terms of judicial ruling (qada') but not in terms of his conscience (diyanah). This distinction is because the imam did not intend to lead, so internally he is not breaking the oath, but in the eyes of the court, the fact that someone followed him makes him a leader. However, if he had witnesses before starting that he is praying alone, then even in judgment he is not a breaker. The passage also applies the same rule to Jumu'ah prayer. The commentary elaborates that intention is hidden and rulings are based on apparent actions, hence the qada' ruling. The text is cut off at the end, but the main ruling is clear.

Key Terms
حانث (hanith): One who breaks an oath
قضاء (qada'): Judicial ruling based on external evidence
ديانة (diyanah): Inner conscience and religious obligation

C) The imam does not break his oath at all.
D) The prayer of the follower is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, oaths are evaluated separately in court (by externals) and in conscience (by intention), and both must be considered when issuing a fatwa.

Ruling on the Imam's Intention for Women's Following with Exceptions
Ruling on imam's intention for women's following with exceptions and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of the imam's intention for women's following, identify the exception for Janazah, and evaluate the ikhtilaf regarding Jumu'ah and Eidain using the maxim 'al-nadir kal-'adam'.

Core Idea
The imam must intend to lead women for valid following in fard 'ayn prayers, except Janazah; Jumu'ah and Eidain are disputed.

This lesson unpacks a rasm al-mufti rule: for women's following to be valid, the imam must specifically intend to lead them. Without this intention, the imam's prayer would be invalid because he takes on a commitment he did not undertake. However, the rule has an exception: Janazah prayer is excluded as it is not a 'complete individual prayer'. Additionally, a scholarly dispute exists whether Jumu'ah and Eid prayers are also exempt. The minority view invokes the maxim 'al-nadir kal-'adam' (the rare is like non-existent), but the majority requires intention for all fard 'ayn prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal rule
The rule: For women's following to be correct, the imam must intend to lead them. Understand the underlying rationale: without this intention, the imam's prayer would become corrupt because he would be committing to a leadership role he did not intend.
This is a preventive measure to avoid invalidity of the imam's prayer.
2
Recognize the exception for Janazah
The rule does not apply to the funeral prayer (Janazah) because it is not a 'fard kamil' (complete individual obligation). Janazah is a fard kifayah, lacking the full structure of a fard 'ayn prayer.
The exception is based on the nature of the prayer itself.
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf regarding Jumu'ah and Eidain
Some jurists exclude Jumu'ah and Eid prayers from the intention requirement. They argue that the harm (fitnah) that necessitates the condition is rare in these large, well-structured congregations, so the maxim 'al-nadir kal-'adam' applies.
The majority holds that the general principle includes all fard 'ayn prayers, including Jumu'ah and Eid.
4
Apply the tarjih mechanism
The author (Ibn Nujaym) corrects the minority view via the Khulasah and declares the majority position as mukhtar (chosen) and mufta bihi.
Thus, in fatwa, the imam must intend to lead women for Jumu'ah and Eidain as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

It will be, whose commitment he did not make himself, and this is against the Shari'ah; therefore, for the correctness of women following, it was deemed necessary for the imam to intend to lead them, so that without his commitment the imam's prayer does not become corrupt. But this ruling does not include the funeral prayer; this ruling is only for those prayers that are a complete individual prayer, and the funeral prayer is not a complete individual prayer, so that no objection occurs. And some excluded Friday and the two Eids: According to the majority of scholars, for the correctness of women following, it is necessary for the imam to intend to lead them, and Friday and Eid prayers are included in this. While according to some jurists, for Friday and Eid, the imam's intention to lead women is not necessary; the reason is that the harm due to which a distinction was made between men and women following is rare in Friday and Eid prayers, and 'the rare is like non-existent' is well-known. The author, citing the Khulasah, corrected the statement of some jurists and declared it the chosen view.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm rule (methodological ruling) regarding the condition of the imam's intention when women join his congregation. The rule: For women's following to be valid, the imam must specifically intend to lead them. Without this intention, the imam's prayer would be invalid because he would be taking on a commitment he did not intend. However, this condition does not apply to the funeral prayer (Janazah), because Janazah is not a complete individual prayer (fard kifayah); it lacks the structure of a full prayer. Some jurists also exclude Friday and Eid prayers, arguing that the harm (fitnah) that necessitates the condition is rare in these large gatherings, and rare is like non-existent. The author of Al-Ashbah (Ibn Nujaym) corrected this minority view via the Khulasah and declared it the relied-upon position (mukhtar). Thus, the majority position includes Friday and Eid.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in prayer
نیت امامت (niyyat imamat): The imam's intention to lead the congregation
فرد کامل (fard kamil): A complete individual prayer (i.e., one that is fard 'ayn)
النادر كالعدم (al-nadir kal-'adam): The rare is like non-existent – a legal maxim used to disregard rare occurrences in legal rulings.

7 min
Oath Not to Lead: Qada’ vs Diyanah
Ruling on oath not to lead: qada’ vs diyanah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qada'/diyanah distinction to an oath not to lead and explain why the swearer breaks judicially but not conscientiously.

Core Idea
The imam's intention is hidden; court rules by appearance, but Allah knows the heart.

When someone swears not to lead prayer and others follow him, the following is valid. But does he break his oath? The answer depends on whether we judge by outward action (qada’) or inner intention (diyanah). This lesson unpacks the juristic reasoning behind the dual ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the oath
The swearer vowed not to lead anyone. A person then follows him in prayer. Determine the validity of the following and whether the oath is broken.
The imam's intention is not a condition for the follower's prayer validity.
2
Distinguish qada’ and diyanah
Qada’ is the outward judicial ruling based on observable evidence; diyanah is the inner reality before Allah. Here, outwardly he led (people followed), but inwardly he had no intention to lead.
This distinction is a hallmark of Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply the rule to the basic scenario
Since intention is hidden, the court rules he broke the oath (qada’an). However, he did not intend to lead, so before Allah he is not a breaker (diyanatan).
Expiation is due in court but not in conscience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ حَلَفَ أَنْ لَا يَؤُمَّ أَحَداً فَاقْتَدَىٰ بِهِ إِنْسَانُ صَحَّ الْاقْتِدَاءُ وَهَلْ يَحْنَثُ قَالَ فِي الْخَانِيَةِ يَحْنَثُ قَضَاءً لَا دِيَانَةً إِلَّا إِذَا أَشْهَدَ قَبْلَ الشُّرُوعِ فَلَا يَحْنَثُ قَضَاءً وَكَذَا لَوْ أَمَّ النَّاسَ هَذَا الْحَالِفُ فِي صَلَاةِ الْجُمُعَةِ صَحَّتْ وَحَنَثَ قَضَاءً. ترجمہ: اور اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ وہ کسی کی امامت نہیں کرے گا اور اس کی کسی آدمی نے اقتداء کر لی تو اقتدا [درست] ہے اور کیا وہ حانث ہو جائے گا ؟ تو خانیہ میں کہا ہے کہ وہ قضاء حانث ہو جائے گا دیانۃً حانث نہ ہو گا مگر جبکہ شروع کرنے سے پہلے گواہ بنالے تو قضاء بھی حانث نہ ہوگا۔ اور ایسے ہی اگر اس قسم کھانے والے نے جمعہ کی نماز میں لوگوں کو امامت کرائی تو امامت صحیح ہے اور قضاء حانث ہو جائیگا۔ تشریح اگر کسی نے امامت نہ کرانے کی قسم کھائی اس کے بعد کسی دن وہ تنہا نماز پڑھ رہا تھا کہ کسی نے آکر اس کے پیچھے اقتداء کی نیت سے ہاتھ باندھ کر نماز میں شرکت کی تو اس کی اقتدا [درست] ہے اور امامت بھی صحیح ہوگئی اقتداء کے لئے تو نیت متابعت ضروری ہے لیکن امام کے لئے نیت امامت شرط نہیں صورت مسئلہ میں امامت کے صحیح ہو جانے کی وجہ سے امام حانث ہو گیا اور امام صاحب پر قسم کا کفارہ واجب ہوگا لیکن یہ حکم قضاء ہے دیانۃً نہیں۔ دیانۃً اس وجہ سے حانث نہیں ہوگا کہ امامت کی نیت نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے امامت کرنا نہیں کہا جائیگا اس لئے قسم کی خلاف ورزی نہیں ہوئی اور وہ حانث نہیں ہوا اور لوگوں نے اس کی اقتداء کی تو ظاہر میں وہ امام بن گیا با نیت کرنا اور نہ کرنا امر پوشیدہ ہے اور امر پوشیدہ پر حکم کا ترتب نہیں ہوتا اس لئے قضاء حانث ہو جائیگا، اگر نماز شروع کرنے سے پہلے اس نے امامت نہ کرنے پر گواہ بنا لئے کہ وہ تنہا نماز پڑھ رہا ہے اور کسی کی امامت نہیں کر رہا ہے اور اس کے بعد کوئی اس کی اقتداء میں ہاتھ باندھ کر کھڑا ہو گیا تو اس صورت میں قضاء بھی حانث نہ ہوگا امامت کی نیت کا نہ ہونا بالکل ظاہر ہو گیا۔ وكذا لو أَمَّ النَّاسَ هَذَا الْحَالِفُ : اگر امام نے امامت نہ کرانے کی قسم کھائی اور پھر اس نے جمعہ کی نماز میں امامت کرادی تو اس صورت میں قضاء ودیانۃً حانث ہو جائیگا اور قضاء اس پر کفارہ واجب ہوگا اس لئے کہ جب اس نے امامت نہ کرانے کی قسم کھائی اور قسم کے بعد جمعہ کی نماز پڑھائی تو یہ اس بات کی علامت ہے کہ وہ قسم توڑنے پر راضی ہوگیا کیونکہ جمعہ کی نماز کم از کم تین مقتدیوں کو تلزم ہے اور اس جگہ اگر وہ امامت شروع کرانے سے پہلے گواہ بھی بنا لے تب بھی حانث ہو جائیگا اور گواہ بنانے کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ ا مصنف نے اس میں حنث قضاء فرمایا جبکہ اس مسئلہ میں قضاء و دیانۃً حانث ہو جائیگا تو تاویل کر کے یوں کہا جاسکتا ہے کہ امامت کے نیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے گویا اس نے امامت نہیں کی اور امامت نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے وہ دیانۃً حانث نہ ہوگا، جیسے کسی نے سفر شرعی نہ کرنے کی قسم کھا رکھی ہے اور وہ گھر سے بلانیت سفر شرعی نکل پڑا تو وہ کتنی ہی دور نکل جائے لیکن وہ دیانۃً حانث نہ ہو گا۔
And if he swore that he will not lead anyone, and a person followed him, the following is valid. And does he break the oath? He said in al-Khaniyah: He breaks it judicially (qada'an) but not conscientiously (diyanatan), unless he called witnesses before starting, then he does not break it judicially. Similarly, if this swearer led people in Friday prayer, it is valid and he breaks the oath judicially. Translation: And if someone swore that he will not lead anyone, and a person followed him, the following is valid. And does he become a breaker of the oath? In al-Khaniyah it is said that he becomes a breaker judicially, not conscientiously, except if he made witnesses before starting, then he does not become a breaker judicially. And similarly, if this swearer led people in Friday prayer, the leading is valid and he becomes a breaker judicially. Explanation: If someone swore not to lead, and later he was praying alone when someone came and stood behind him with the intention of following, his following is valid and the leading also became valid. For following, intention of following is necessary, but for the imam, intention of leading is not a condition. In this scenario, due to the validity of leading, the imam became a breaker of the oath and the oath-holder owes expiation, but this ruling is judicial, not conscientious. Conscientiously he will not become a breaker because without intention of leading, it is not called leading; thus there is no violation of the oath and he is not a breaker. People followed him, so outwardly he became an imam; intention or lack thereof is a hidden matter, and a hidden matter does not result in a ruling, so judicially he becomes a breaker. If before starting prayer he called witnesses that he is praying alone and not leading anyone, and then someone came and stood with folded hands following him, then in that case judicially he also does not become a breaker, because the absence of intention of leading became completely apparent. And similarly, if this swearer led people: if the imam swore not to lead and then led people in Friday prayer, then in that case he becomes a breaker both judicially and conscientiously, and expiation is obligatory upon him judicially, because when he swore not to lead and after the oath led Friday prayer, this is a sign that he agreed to break the oath, since Friday prayer requires at least three followers. And in this case, even if he made witnesses before starting to lead, he still becomes a breaker and the witnessing is not considered. The author (of al-Ashbah) ruled that he breaks judicially, but in this issue he breaks both judicially and conscientiously, so it can be interpreted that due to the absence of intention of leading, he effectively did not lead, and due to not leading, he does not break conscientiously, just like someone who swore not to undertake a shar'i journey and left home without intention of a shar'i journey, even if he goes far, he does not break conscientiously.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage discusses a rasm rule concerning oaths related to leading prayer. The core issue: If a person swears not to lead anyone in prayer, and someone follows him, what is the ruling? The following is valid because the imam's intention is not a condition for validity. However, the oath-breaker (hanth) is considered broken judicially (qada'an) in a court of law, but not conscientiously (diyanatan) before Allah, because he did not intend to lead. The exception is if he called witnesses before starting that he is praying alone; then even judicially he is not considered to have broken the oath, as his lack of intention is manifest. For Friday prayer, the ruling is stricter: since Friday requires a congregation of at least three followers, leading it is considered a clear act of leading, so he breaks the oath both judicially and conscientiously, and witnessing before starting does not help. The author (Ibn Nujaym) notes that the ruling in al-Ashbah mentions only qada'an for Friday, but the correct view is that he breaks both; he then offers a ta'wil (interpretation) that perhaps the author meant that due to lack of intention, he does not break diyanatan. An analogy is given: a person who swears not to undertake a shar'i journey (travel for which concessions are allowed) and leaves home without intending such a journey does not break the oath conscientiously even if he goes far.

Key Terms
یمین (yamin): An oath; a binding promise made by swearing by Allah
حنث (hanth): Breaking an oath; incurring the obligation of expiation
قضاء (qada'an): Judicially; according to apparent evidence in court
دیانۃ (diyanatan): Conscientiously; according to what one knows internally before Allah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in the basic scenario (swearer does not call witnesses), what is the ruling on the oath?
A) He breaks the oath both qada'an and diyanatan
B) He breaks qada'an but not diyanatan
C) He does not break qada'an but breaks diyanatan
D) He does not break the oath at all

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, outward acts determine judicial rulings; inner states matter before Allah alone.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
7 min
Exceptions: Witnesses and Friday Prayer
Exceptions to the qada'/diyanah rule: witnesses and Friday prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the two exceptions to the qada'/diyanah rule: calling witnesses (no qada' breach) and Friday prayer (both qada' and diyanah breach).

Core Idea
Calling witnesses proves lack of intention; leading Friday prayer is always a clear breach.

The previous lesson established that an unintentional following results in qada' but not diyanah breach. However, two important exceptions modify this rule: if the swearer calls witnesses before starting that he is praying alone, he avoids even the qada' breach. And if he leads Friday prayer, he breaks both qada'an and diyanatan, because Friday requires a congregation. This lesson examines these exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Examine the witness exception
If the swearer calls witnesses before starting that he is praying alone, and then someone follows him, he does not break the oath even qada'an. Why? Because his lack of intention is now manifest.
The witnesses make his intention publicly known, so the court cannot presume he led.
2
Analyze the Friday prayer scenario
If the swearer leads Friday prayer, he breaks the oath both qada'an and diyanatan. Friday prayer requires at least three followers, so leading it is a clear act of leadership, implying consent to break the oath.
Witnesses do not help here; the act itself is conclusive.
3
Contrast the two exceptions
The witness exception removes the qada' ruling; the Friday exception adds the diyanah ruling. The difference lies in the nature of the act: Friday prayer is inherently congregational, so intention is presumed.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage discusses a rasm rule concerning oaths related to leading prayer. The core issue: If a person swears not to lead anyone in prayer, and someone follows him, what is the ruling? The following is valid because the imam's intention is not a condition for validity. Key Terms
إشهاد (ishhad): Calling witnesses to testify that one is not leading.
صلاة الجمعة (salat al-jumu'ah): Friday congregational prayer, wajib with at least 3 followers.

Exceptions for Janazah and Sajdah Tilawah from Oath
Ruling that funeral prayer and prostration of recitation are excluded from the general oath not to lead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the exceptions from an absolute oath not to lead prayer, state the legal reasoning, and apply the ruling to funeral prayer and prostration of recitation.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer and prostration of recitation are not 'absolute prayer' for oaths, so leading them does not break an oath.

Oaths in Islamic law are interpreted according to customary and shari'i meanings. If someone swears not to lead, the default is that leading a standard prayer (with ruku' and sujud) would break the oath. However, this passage from Sharh al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair introduces two key exceptions: funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) and prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah). Understanding these exceptions is crucial for muftis to correctly advise on the validity of oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
An absolute oath not to lead (yamin mutlaq) refers to leading a complete prayer (salat) in its usual form.
The default meaning of 'salat' in oaths is the five daily prayers or any prayer with ruku' and sujud.
2
Note the first exception: funeral prayer
Leading salat al-janazah does not break the oath because it lacks the typical structure (no ruku' or sujud) and is considered a fard kifayah, not a normal salat.
The text states 'salat al-janazah does not fall under mutlaq salah'.
3
Note the second exception: prostration of recitation
Leading sajdat al-tilawah also does not break the oath because it is not considered 'leading' in the absolute sense; it is a separate act of worship.
The reasoning is analogous: it is outside the absolute meaning of 'imamah' in the oath.
4
Apply the same reasoning to the specific person case
If a person swears not to lead a specific individual and leads a congregation intending to exclude him, but that individual joins, the oath is broken even if the imam is unaware. This shows that the oath's scope includes the act of leading, not the imam's intent alone.
The text distinguishes this from the exceptions: here the act of leading still occurs, so the oath is broken, but no reward is earned.
5
Conclude the practical fatwa
A mufti should rule that no expiation is required for leading funeral prayer or prostration of recitation under an absolute oath, but expiation is required if the oath is broken by leading a regular prayer or if a specific person joins despite intent to exclude.
These rulings are based on Fatawa Qadikhan as cited in Sharh al-Ashbah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَحْنَثُ أَصْلًا إِذَا أَمَّهُمْ فِي صَلَاةِ الْجَنَازَةِ وَسَجْدَةِ التِّلَاوَةِ. ترجمہ: اور بالکل حانث نہ ہو گا جبکہ اس نے ان کی امامت کی ہو نماز جنازہ اور سجدہ تلاوت میں ۔ تشریح اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ وہ امامت نہیں کرے گا اس کے بعد اس نے نماز جنازہ پڑھادی تو قسم کھانے والا اپنی قسم میں حانث نہ ہو گا علامہ حمومی نے شرح اشباہ میں فتاوی قاضیخاں کے حوالہ سے ذکر کیا ہے کہ جب اس نے مطلق قسم کھائی ہے تو اس کی یمین مطلق نماز کی طرف لوٹے گی اور وہ فرض یا نفل نماز ہے نماز جنازہ مطلق نماز کے تحت نہیں آتی لہذا ایسا شخص حانث نہ ہوگا ۔ وسجدة التلاوة: اگر امام نے امامت نہ کرنے کی قسم کھائی اس کے بعد سجدہ تلاوت میں امام بن گیا تو وہ حانث نہ ہوگا اور اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں کیونکہ اس نے مطلق امامت نہ کرنے کی قسم کھائی ہے تو اسے مطلق امامت کی طرف پھیرا جائیگا اور سجدہ تلاوت اس اطلاق سے باہر ہے۔ وَلَوْ حَلَفَ أَنْ لَا يَؤُمَّ فُلَاناً فَأَمَّ النَّاسَ نَاوِياً أَنْ لَا يَؤُمَّهُ وَيَؤُمَّ غَيْرَهُ فَاقْتَدَىٰ بِهِ فُلَانٌ حَنَثَ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَعْلَمْ بِهِ انْتَهَىٰ وَلَكِنْ لَا ثَوَابَ لَهُ عَلَى الْإِمَامَةِ وَسُجُودِ التِّلَاوَةِ كَالصَّلَاةِ. ترجمہ: اور اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ وہ فلاں شخص کی امامت نہیں کرے گا اور اس نے لوگوں کی امامت کی یہ نیت کرتے ہوئے کہ اس کی امامت نہیں کرے گا اور اس کے علاوہ کی امامت کرے گا پس اس فلاں نے اس کی اقتداء کر لی تو وہ حانث ہو جائیگا اگر چہ وہ اسے جانتا بھی نہ ہو لیکن نماز کی طرح اس کو امامت پر ثواب نہیں ملے گا اور سجدہ تلاوت نماز کی طرح ہے۔
And he does not break the oath at all when he leads them in the funeral prayer and the prostration of recitation. Translation: And he will absolutely not become a breaker of the oath when he has led them in the funeral prayer and the prostration of recitation. Explanation: If someone swore that he will not lead, and then he led the funeral prayer, the swearer will not become a breaker of his oath. Allamah Hammawi in Sharh al-Ashbah, citing Fatawa Qadikhan, mentioned that when he swore an absolute oath, his oath refers to absolute prayer, and that is obligatory or supererogatory prayer; the funeral prayer does not fall under absolute prayer, therefore such a person will not become a breaker. And the prostration of recitation: If the imam swore not to lead and then became an imam in the prostration of recitation, he does not become a breaker and expiation is not obligatory, because he swore not to lead absolutely, so it is referred to absolute leading, and the prostration of recitation is outside that absoluteness. And if he swore that he will not lead so-and-so, and he led the people intending not to lead him and to lead others, and then that so-and-so followed him, he breaks the oath even if he was unaware of him, but there is no reward for him for leading, and the prostration of recitation is like prayer.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage provides exceptions to the rule that leading prayer breaks an oath not to lead. First, the funeral prayer (Salat al-Janazah) is not considered 'prayer' in the absolute sense (mutlaq salah) because it is a fard kifayah and lacks the usual structure; thus, leading it does not break an absolute oath. Second, the prostration of recitation (Sajdah Tilawah) is also excluded; it is not considered 'leading' in the absolute sense, so the oath is not broken. Then, a separate case: if a person swears not to lead a specific individual, and he leads a congregation intending not to lead that person, but that person joins, he breaks the oath even if he was unaware of his presence. However, he receives no reward for leading in that case. The prostration of recitation is analogized to prayer in this context (i.e., the same ruling applies to leading it with respect to reward).

Key Terms
صلاة الجنازة (salat al-janazah): Funeral prayer; a prayer with no ruku' or sujud, performed standing
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration of recitation; a single prostration that is wajib upon reciting certain verses
یمین مطلق (yamin mutlaq): An absolute oath without qualification

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because he led a prayer
B) No, because funeral prayer is not considered absolute prayer
C) Yes, but only qada'an
D) No, unless he intended to lead

Key Takeaway
Janazah and Sajdah Tilawah are not considered absolute prayer or leading in oaths, so they do not trigger a broken oath.

Ruling on Sujood al-Shukr (Prostration of Thanks)
Clarifies that sujood al-shukr is not wajib and gives public/private guidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sujood al-shukr and apply the principle of sadd al-dhara'i to determine the appropriate context for its performance.

Core Idea
Sujood al-shukr is not wajib; public performance risks misinterpretation as obligatory.

This passage addresses a common question about the legal status of sujood al-shukr in the Hanafi madhhab. While some may assume it is wajib, Imam Abu Hanifa clarified it is not. The text also provides practical guidance for the mufti: avoid public performance to prevent laypeople from mistakenly considering it fard or wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognise that sujood al-shukr is a prostration of thanks. The passage negates wujub, meaning it is not obligatory.
The ruling is about legal obligation, not permissibility.
2
Understand the rationale behind the caution
The text advises against public performance to prevent people from thinking it is fard or wajib. This reflects the principle of sadd al-dhara'i (blocking means to evil).
The concern is about misconception, not prohibition of the act itself.
3
Apply the ruling to public vs. private contexts
In private, there is no harm. In public, it is better to avoid to uphold the correct understanding of obligations.
The distinction is based on potential harm, not intrinsic nature of the act.
4
Note the relevance for a mufti
A mufti should advise according to this ruling, emphasizing the non-obligatory status and contextual caution.
This guidance is part of Rasm al-Mufti (etiquette and method of issuing fatwas).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

It is narrated that it negates the obligation of sujood al-shukr, meaning that according to Imam Sahib (Abu Hanifa), sujood al-shukr is not wajib. (For details, see Umdat al-Idah Sharh Nur al-Idah, vol. 2, p. 36). One should avoid performing sujood al-shukr in a public gathering so that people do not come to consider it as fard or wajib. If someone performs it in private, there is no harm.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling (hukm) regarding sujood al-shukr (prostration of thanks). The author states that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, sujood al-shukr is not wajib (obligatory). The text then gives practical guidance: it is better to avoid performing this prostration in public to prevent laypeople from mistakenly believing it is fard or wajib. However, if performed in private, there is no prohibition. This advice reflects the principle of sadd al-dhara’i (blocking means to evil) and the importance of preserving correct understanding of religious obligations.

Key Terms
سجدہ شکر (sajdah shukr): Prostration of thanks, performed upon receiving a blessing or being saved from calamity.
وجوب (wujub): Legal obligation; here it negates the wajib status of sujood al-shukr.

Intention as a Condition for I'tikaf
States that intention is necessary for all types of i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rasm al-mufti rule that intention is a condition for all types of i'tikaf, and differentiate the requirement for fasting between wajib/sunnah and nafl i'tikaf.

Core Idea
Intention is the universal condition for every valid i'tikaf, but fasting is only required for wajib and sunnah.

As a mufti, you must know the conditions that govern i'tikaf. This lesson establishes a foundational rasm al-mufti rule: intention is a necessary condition for all types of i'tikaf. However, the requirement for fasting differs, which is crucial for issuing correct fatwas on i'tikaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its types
The text defines i'tikaf and lists three types: wajib (by vow), sunnah mu'akkadah, and nafl. Recognize each category.
2
State the intention rule
Intention (niyyah) is a condition for validity in all three types. No i'tikaf is valid without it.
3
State the fasting rule
Fasting is a condition only for sunnah and wajib i'tikaf, not for nafl. This is a key distinction.
4
Apply to a fatwa scenario
If a person asks about nafl i'tikaf, you must rule that intention is needed but fasting is not. For sunnah/wajib, both are required.
5
Note the authority
This rule is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as recorded in classical texts like Nur al-Izah and Fatawa al-Nawazil.
Authority: zahir_riwayah

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الاعتكاف فهي شرط صحته واجبا كان أو سنة أو نفلا. ترجمه اور بہر حال اعتکاف پس وہ اس کی صحت کی شرط ہے خواہ اعتکاف واجب ہو یا سنت یا نفل۔ تشريح : الاعتكاف لغة لزوم الشئ وحبس النفس عليه وفى الشريعة هو اللبث في المسجده مع الصوم ونية الاعتكاف وفي فتاوى النوازل الاعتكاف هو اللبث في المسجد للعبادة على وجه مخصوص (عمدۃ الایضاح شرح اردو نور الایضاح ج ۲ ص ۳۶۵) اعتکاف کی تین قسمیں ہیں (۱) واجب (۲) نفل (۳) سنت مؤکدہ ۔ اول الذکر بندہ کے واجب کرنے سے ہوتا ہے مؤخر الذکر دونوں اللہ کی طرف سے ہیں اعتکاف کی اقسام ثلثہ میں سے ہر ایک کے اندر نیت شرط ہے نیز اعتکاف سنت اور اعتکاف واجب میں روزہ شرط ہے اور اعتکاف نفل میں روزہ شرط نہیں ہے۔
As for i'tikaf, intention is a condition for its validity, whether it is obligatory or sunnah or nafl. Translation: In any case, i'tikaf, it is a condition for its validity, regardless of whether i'tikaf is obligatory, sunnah, or nafl. Explanation: I'tikaf linguistically means clinging to something and confining oneself to it. In Sharia it is staying in the mosque with fasting and intention of i'tikaf. In Fatawa al-Nawazil, i'tikaf is staying in the mosque for worship in a specific manner. There are three types of i'tikaf: (1) obligatory, (2) nafl, (3) sunnah mu'akkadah. The first is made obligatory by the servant's vow; the latter two are from Allah. Among the three types of i'tikaf, intention is a condition in each. Also, in sunnah and obligatory i'tikaf, fasting is a condition, but in nafl i'tikaf, fasting is not a condition.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage establishes a rasm rule: intention (niyyah) is a necessary condition for the validity of i'tikaf in all its forms. The text first states the rule in Arabic, then explains it in Urdu. It clarifies that i'tikaf has three types: wajib (by vow), sunnah mu'akkadah (the ten days of Ramadan), and nafl (voluntary). For all, intention is required. However, for sunnah and wajib i'tikaf, fasting is also a condition, while for nafl i'tikaf, fasting is not required. This is a Hanafi position derived from the definition of i'tikaf in Sharia, which includes staying in the mosque with intention and fasting for non-nafl types. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as it follows the classical definitions in works like Nur al-Izah and Fatawa al-Nawazil.

Key Terms
الاعتكاف (al-i'tikaf): Staying in the mosque with intention and fasting for the sake of worship
النِّيَّة (al-niyyah): Intention, a condition for validity of i'tikaf in all forms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wajib i'tikaf
B) Sunnah i'tikaf
C) Nafl i'tikaf
D) All require fasting

Key Takeaway
Intention is a necessary condition for all forms of i'tikaf; fasting is only required for wajib and sunnah i'tikaf.
