Intention as a Condition for Kaffarat
States a rasm al-mufti rule: intention is a condition for all kaffarat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that intention is required for all forms of kaffarat and state the additional condition of night intention for fasting expiations.

Core Idea
Intention is required for all expiations; fasting expiation requires night intention.

This lesson examines a fundamental rule of fatwa: intention (niyyah) is a condition for the validity of expiations (kaffarat). The source makes clear that this applies equally whether the expiation is freeing a slave, feeding the poor, or fasting. An important additional requirement is stated for fasting: the intention must be made at night, mirroring the rule for obligatory fasts. Muftis must apply this rule when assessing the validity of an expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is kaffarat (expiations). The ruling is that intention is a condition (shart) for their validity.
Intention is a shart, not a rukn, but its absence invalidates the act.
2
Recognize the three forms of kaffarat
The text mentions three forms: freeing a slave (itq), fasting (sawm), and feeding (it'am). All require intention.
3
Note the special condition for fasting kaffarah
When the kaffarah is performed through fasting, the intention must be made at night (before dawn). This is additional to the general requirement.
This follows the rule for obligatory fasts (sawm al-fard).
4
Understand the principle behind the rule
The commentary explains that kaffarat are 'among the intended acts of worship' (ibadat maqsuda). Acts of worship require intention to distinguish them from habits.
5
Apply in fatwa practice
When asked about the validity of an expiation, a mufti must first confirm that the person had intention at the time of the act. If it was fasting, the intention must have been made at night.
If intention is missing, the expiation must be repeated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكفارات فالنية شرط صحتها عنقا أو صياما أو إطعاما. ترجمه اور رہے کفارات پس نیت ان کے صحیح ہونے کی شرط ہے خواہ آزادی ہو یا روزہ یا کھانا کھلانا۔ تشريح: كفاره بھی عبادات مقصودہ میں سے ہے لہذا اس کی صحت کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے خواہ کفارہ غلام آزاد کرنے کی صورت میں ہو یا مساکین کو کھانا کھلانے کی صورت میں یا روزہ رکھنے کی صورت میں، کفارہ کی ہر قسم کی صحت کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے، بدون نیت کفارہ صحیح نہ ہوگا، البتہ جب کفارہ روزہ کی شکل میں ادا کیا جائیگا تو پھر اس میں رات ہی کو نیت کرنا ضروری ہوگا. Explanation: Kaffarah is among the intended acts of worship; therefore, intention is necessary for its validity, whether the expiation is in the form of freeing a slave, feeding the poor, or fasting. Intention is necessary for the validity of every type of expiation; without intention the expiation will not be valid. However, when the expiation is performed in the form of fasting, then it is necessary to make the intention at night.

Commentary
This passage continues the series of rulings on intention, now focusing on kaffarat (expiations). The rule states that intention is a condition for the validity of any kaffarah, whether it involves freeing a slave, fasting, or feeding the poor. The Urdu commentary emphasizes that without intention, the expiation is invalid. It adds an important qualification: when the kaffarah is through fasting, the intention must be made at night (before dawn), following the general rule for obligatory fasts. This is from the Hanafi school, as noted in the hashiyah. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as the rule is standard.

Key Terms
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): An expiatory act required for certain violations (e.g., breaking an oath or fasting in Ramadan)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Intention for Sacrifice: At Purchase or Slaughter? A Rasm al-Mufti Rule
States rule + derived case on unauthorized slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that intention for udhiyah is at purchase, and evaluate the derived case of unauthorized slaughter to determine the validity of the sacrifice and liability.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, intention for the sacrifice is fixed at purchase — the initial niyyah carries through to slaughter.

This lesson examines a rasm al-mufti rule regarding the timing of intention (niyyah) for udhiyah. While other schools require intention at the moment of slaughter, the Hanafi school holds that intention at the time of purchase is sufficient. The text then derives a specific case: if someone buys an animal with sacrifice in mind, and another person slaughters it without permission, the validity of the sacrifice depends on whether the buyer holds the slaughterer liable. Understanding this ruling helps muftis determine the operative position and its applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
State the rule: intention for udhiyah is obligatory at purchase, not at slaughter. This is the core principle.
The phrase 'عند الشراء لا عند الذبح' is the key.
2
Understand the Proof
Note the analogy (qiyas) with zakat: intention at separation suffices. The initial intention carries through the complete act.
Hanafi usul: intention at the beginning of a continuous act suffices.
3
Trace the Derivation
Follow the tafri' (derivation): if someone buys with intention and another slaughters without permission, the rule branches into two scenarios based on liability.
The text uses 'وتفرع عليه' to introduce the subsidiary case.
4
Distinguish the Scenarios
Two outcomes: (1) Buyer takes the animal and does not hold liable → sacrifice valid for buyer. (2) Buyer holds liable → sacrifice valid for the slaughterer. If slaughterer intends for owner, no liability.
The key variable is whether the buyer demands compensation (daman).
5
Apply the Rule
Use the mufta bihi position: the operative stance is from al-Dhakhirah. In fatwa, the mufti relies on the initial intention at purchase.
Authority: al-Dhakhirah is a Zahir al-Riwayah text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الضحايا فلا بد فيها من النية لكن عند الشراء لا عند الذبح. وتفرع عليه أنه لو اشتراها بنية الأضحية فذبحها غيره بلا إذن فإن أخذها مذبوحا حقا ولم يضمنه أجزأه وإن ضمنه لا تجزيه كما في أضحية الذخيرة. وهذا إذا ذبحها عن نفسه وأما إذا ذبحها عن مالكها فلا ضمان عليه. ترجمه اور میں قربانیاں تو ان میں نیت ضروری ہے لیکن خریدنے کے وقت نہ کہ ذبح کے وقت اور اسی پر متفرع ہے کہ اگر اسکو قربانی کی نیت سے خریدا پھر کسی دوسرے نے بغیر اجازت کے ذبح کر دیا پس اگر اس نے ذبح شده لے لیا اور اسکو ضامن قرار نہیں دیا تو اسکو کافی ہے۔ اور اگر اسکو ضامن قرار دیا تو اس کو کافی نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ ذخیرہ کے کتاب الاضحیۃ میں ایسا ہی ہے۔ اور یہ اس صورت میں ہے کہ جب اسکو اپنی طرف سے ذبح کیا اور بہر حال جب اسکو اسکے مالک کی طرف سے ذبح کیا تو اسپر ضمان نہیں۔ تشريح: بذل الحمود میں اس میں چار افات لکھتے ہیں اضحیه (بضم الهمزه) إضحيه ( بكسر الهمزه) اس کی اضاحی ہے ضحیۃ اس کی جمع ضحایا ہے اور اضحاۃ اس کی جمع اضحا ہے۔و فی الدر المختار: الأضحية لغةً إسم لما يذبح أيام الأضحى من تسمية الشئ بإسم وقته. وقال الكرخي: وهي ما يذبح يوم العيد تقرباً إلى الله تعالى وسميت بذالك لأنها تفعل لأضحى. قربانی بھی عبادت مقصود ہے اس لئے اسکی صحت کیلئے نیت ضروری ہے۔ لیکن عند الشراء لاعند الذبیح اس سے اگر چہ ی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ نیت خریدنے کے وقت ضروری ہے ذبح کے وقت نہیں حالانکہ اصل یہ ہے کہ ذبح کے وقت نیت ضروری ھے اور اگر خریدنے کے وقت بھی نیت کر لی تو وہ نیت بھی کافی ہے جیسے زکوۃ دیتے وقت نیت ضروری ہے لیکن اگر مال زکوۃ کو علاحدہ کرتے وقت نیت کرلی اور دیتے وقت زکوۃ کی نیت نہ کرے تو کافی ہے۔ علامہ ابن نجیم تفریع پیش کرتے ہوئے تحریر کرتے ہیں۔ کہ اگر کسی نے جانور کو خریدتے وقت قربانی کی نیت کی پھر کسی دوسرے آدمی نے مالک کی دلالہ یا صراحہ اجازت کے بغیر اسکو اپنی طرف سے ذبح کر دیا تو اب دو صورتیں ہیں کہ خریدنے والا ذبح کئے ہوئے جانور کو لے لے اور اسے ضامن نہ بنائے ۔ دوسری صورت میں اس مذبوحہ جانور کو نہ لے اور اسے ضامن بنالے، پہلی صورت میں قربانی جانور خریدنے والے کی طرف سے ہوگی اور دوسری صورت میں خود ذابح کی طرف سے قربانی ہو جائیگی۔ لیکن اگر ذابح نے جانور خود مالک ہی کی طرف سے ذبح کیا ہے تو اس صورت میں ذابح پر تاوان نہ ہوگا ۔ چونکہ ان مسائل میں قربانی کی نیت جانور کے خریدتے وقت ہی کر لی گئی تھی وہی کافی ہو جاتی ہے بوقت ذبح نیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہوتا۔ لكن عند الشراء: جانوروں کے خریدنے کے وقت نیت کا اعتبار ہے۔ اس کا ثمرہ اس صورت میں ظاہر ہوگا کہ جب کسی نے قربانی کی نیت سے کوئی جانور خریدا پھر اس نے یا کسی اور نے مالک کی اجازت کے بغیر اسے بغیر نیت ذبح کے ذبح کر ڈالا تو اس جانور کی قربانی درست ہو جائے گی اور خرید نے کے وقت کی نیت کافی ہوگی لیکن اگر خریدتے وقت قربانی کی نیت نہیں کی پھر اسی نے یا کسی اور نے بغیر ذبح کی نیت کے ذبح کر ڈالا تو قربانی درست نہ ہوگی۔ تفریح میں جو دوسری صورت ہے اور اس میں ذابح کو ضامن بنایا گیا ہے عقلاً اس کو ضامن بنانا درست نہیں ہونا چاہئے تھا کیونکہ جب بوقت شراء جانور کے مالک نے قربانی کی نیت سے جانور خریدا اور کسی دوسرے نے بغیر مالک جانور کے جانور ذبح کر ڈالا تو جس وقت اس غیر نے جانور کو ذبح کیا ہے اس وقت تو مالک جانور کی ملکیت میں وہ جانور ذبح ہوا اور بوقت شراء قربانی کی نیت پائی ہی گئی جو قربانی کے لئے کافی ہے تو اس غیر پر تاوان کو لازم کرنا درست نہیں ہونا چاہئے تھا۔
As for sacrifices, intention is necessary in them, but at the time of purchase, not at the time of slaughter. And derived from this is that if he bought it with the intention of sacrifice, then someone else slaughtered it without permission, then if he takes it as slaughtered correctly and does not hold him liable, it suffices him; if he holds him liable, it does not suffice him, as in the sacrifice of the Dhakhirah. This is when he slaughtered it for himself; as for when he slaughtered it for its owner, there is no liability upon him. Translation: As for sacrifices, intention is necessary in them, but at the time of purchase, not at the time of slaughter. And upon this is derived that if he bought it with the intention of sacrifice, then someone else slaughtered it without permission, then if he took the slaughtered animal and did not hold him liable, it suffices him. And if he held him liable, it does not suffice him. As in the book of Udhiyah in al-Dhakhirah. This is when he slaughtered it for himself; in any case, when he slaughtered it for its owner, there is no liability upon him. Explanation: ... (Urdu commentary further explains that the intention at purchase is sufficient, and discusses the case where the buyer takes the slaughtered animal without holding the slaughterer liable, then it counts as his sacrifice; if he holds liable, the sacrifice counts for the slaughterer. If the slaughterer intended for the owner, no liability.)
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm rule regarding the intention (niyyah) for udhiyah (sacrifice): the intention is required at the time of purchasing the animal, not at the time of slaughter. The author then derives (tafari') a case: if someone buys an animal with the intention of sacrifice, and another person slaughters it without permission, two scenarios arise: (1) If the buyer takes the slaughtered animal and does not hold the slaughterer liable, the sacrifice is valid for the buyer. (2) If the buyer holds the slaughterer liable (i.e., demands compensation), the sacrifice is not valid for the buyer; instead, it counts for the slaughterer. However, if the slaughterer slaughters intending it for the owner, there is no liability. The Urdu tashreeh elaborates, comparing to zakat where intention at the time of setting aside suffices. The Hanafi position is that intention at purchase is sufficient, and this ruling is found in al-Dhakhirah (a Hanafi work). The commentary also discusses a potential objection: if the buyer already had intention, why hold the slaughterer liable? It explains that the school's ruling is as stated.

Key Terms
الأضحية (al-udhiyah): The animal sacrificed on the days of Eid al-Adha
تفريع (tafri'): Derivation of a subsidiary ruling from a principle
ضمنه (damanahu): Holding someone liable for compensation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the unauthorized slaughter case, under which condition does the sacrifice count for the buyer?
A) The buyer immediately claims the meat
B) The buyer does not hold the slaughterer liable
C) The buyer renews his intention at slaughter
D) The slaughterer had no intention

Key Takeaway
Intention for udhiyah is fixed at purchase; in unauthorized slaughter, the buyer's liability choice determines validity.

Specification of Udhiyah by Intention: Poor vs Rich
Ruling on specification by intention with practical differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm rule that intention absolutely specifies the sacrificial animal for both poor and rich, and state the practical consequence (thamarah) regarding replacement.

Core Idea
Intention alone specifies the udhiyah animal for everyone; the rich must replace if lost, the poor need not.

This lesson examines a rasm al-mufti rule from the Hanafi tradition: does buying an animal with the intention of udhiyah make it legally specified (mutayyan)? The initial view distinguished between a poor and a rich buyer, but the sahih (correct) position establishes absolute specification. Understanding this rule is essential for muftis when asked about selling, replacing, or donating an intended sacrificial animal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
The central question: if someone buys an animal explicitly intending it for udhiyah (sacrifice), does that animal become legally specified solely by that intention?
Specification means the animal is earmarked for the sacrifice; it cannot be used for other purposes.
2
Parse the Initial View
According to some Hanafi authorities, the ruling depends on the buyer's wealth: if faqir (poor), the intention makes the animal specified like a vow (nadhr); if ghani (rich), it does not.
For the poor, the intention is akin to a vow; for the rich, they are already obligated, so intention does not add specification.
3
Understand the Evidence
The initial view's basis: a poor person is not obliged to sacrifice, so his intention is voluntary, similar to a nadhr. A rich person is already obliged, so his intention does not change the animal's status.
The majority of Hanafi scholars hold that a vow can be made by mere intention without verbal utterance, supporting the poor's specification.
4
Recognize the Sahih Tarjih
The correct (sahih) view is that intention absolutely specifies the animal, regardless of wealth. The 'fruit of the difference' (thamarah) lies in the consequences when the animal is lost or destroyed.
The sahih view is the mufta bihi (operative for fatwa).
5
Apply the Thamarah
If the animal is lost before sacrifice: the poor need not replace it; the rich must replace and sacrifice another. If the lost animal is later found after replacement: the poor must sacrifice both; the rich sacrifices only one (without specification), though it is better to sacrifice both.
The difference stems from the nature of obligation: the poor's intention is like a nadhr (does not obligate replacement if lost), while the rich's intention obligates replacement because the original was specified.

Source Text

تشریح : اس عبارت میں نیت پر تفریح پیش کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر قربانی کی نیت سے کوئی جانور خریدا تو وہ جانور متعین ہو جائے گا یا نہیں تو فرمایا کہ فقہاء نے مالدار اور غریب کے مابین فرق کو واضح کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ اگر قربانی کی نیت سے جانور کو خریدنے والا غریب ہے تو وہ جانور قربانی کے لئے متعین ہو جائے گا اور اس غریب کے لئے اس جانور کوفروخت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ غریب کے حق میں یہ بشکل نذر کے ہے اور نذر کی صورت میں منذور چیز متعین ہو جاتی ہے اگر چہ بعض علماء کہتے ہیں کہ نذر کے لئے زبان سے الفاظ ادا کرنا ضروری ہیں لیکن یہ رائے جمہور علماء کے خلاف ہے صرف ارادہ کرنے سے بھی نذر ہو جاتی ہے۔
اور اگر جانور کو خریدنے والا مالدار ہے اور قربانی کی نیت سے جانور خریدا ہے تو وہ جانور قربانی کے لئے متعین نہیں ہوگا۔ ثمرہ اختلاف اس صورت میں ظاہر ہوگا کہ اگر غریب کا جانور گم ہو گیا یا مر گیا تو اس پر دوسرا جانور خرید کر اس کی قربانی ضروری نہیں ہے جب کہ مالدار پر دوسرا جانور خرید کر قربانی کرنا ضروری سے پھر اگر گمشدہ جانور مل جائے اور انہوں نے دوسرا جانور بھی خرید لیا ہو تو غریب پر دونوں جانوروں کی قربانی ضروری ہے جبکہ مالدار پر صرف ایک کی لاعلی التعیین قربانی کرنا ضروری ہوگا اگر چہ بہتر اس کے لئے بھی یہی ہے کہ دونوں جانوروں کی قربانی کرے۔ والصحيح انها تعیین : لیکن قول صحیح یہ ہے کہ قربانی کی نیت سے خریدنے کی صورت میں وہ جانور متعین ہو جا تا ہے خرید نے والا غریب ہو یا مالدار البتہ تعین میں تھوڑا سا فرق ہے جیسے ایک آدمی نے کہا کہ اگر میرا فلاں کام ہوگیا
And does the sacrificial animal become specified by intention? They said: If he is poor and buys it with intention, it becomes specified, so he may not sell it; and if he is rich, it does not become specified. And the correct opinion is that it becomes specified absolutely, so the rich person will give it in charity alive after its days, but he may substitute another in its place, as in al-Bada'i' from the book of Udhiyah. They said: Gifts (hadaya) are like sacrifices.
Translation: And does the sacrificial animal become specified by intention? The jurists say that if he is poor and buys it with intention of sacrifice, then it becomes specified, so selling it is not valid for him; and if he is rich, it does not become specified. And according to the correct opinion, it becomes specified absolutely. So after the days of sacrifice, the rich person will give it in charity alive, but he has permission to put another in its place, as in al-Bada'i' from the book of Udhiyah. The jurists say that gifts are like sacrifices.
Tashrih: In this passage, discussing intention, he says: If someone buys an animal with intention of sacrifice, does that animal become specified or not? He said that the jurists clarified the difference between the rich and poor. They said that if the buyer is poor and buys the animal with intention of sacrifice, then it becomes specified for sacrifice, and it is not permissible for that poor person to sell it, because for the poor it is in the form of a vow (nadhr), and in the case of a vow, the vowed thing becomes specified. Even though some scholars say that for a vow it is necessary to utter words with the tongue, but this opinion is against the majority; just by intention a vow is made.
And if the buyer is rich and buys the animal with intention of sacrifice, then it does not become specified for sacrifice. The fruit of the difference appears in this scenario: if the poor person's animal gets lost or dies, then it is not necessary for him to buy another and sacrifice it, while it is necessary for the rich person to buy another and sacrifice it. Then if the lost animal is found and they have already bought another, then on the poor person it is necessary to sacrifice both animals, while on the rich person it is necessary to sacrifice only one without specification, although it is better for him too to sacrifice both. And the correct is that it becomes specified: but the correct statement is that when buying with intention of sacrifice, the animal becomes specified, whether the buyer is poor or rich; however, there is a slight difference in specification. For example, a person said: 'If my such-and-such work is completed...' (incomplete).
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm rule (ruling) concerning the specification (tayayyun) of the sacrificial animal by intention. The initial view distinguishes between a poor and a rich person: the poor's animal becomes specified like a vow (nadhr), so he cannot sell it; the rich's animal does not become specified. However, the correct (sahih) view is that it becomes specified absolutely for both. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that if the animal is lost, the poor need not replace it (since it was like a vow), but the rich must. If both are lost and then found, the poor must sacrifice both, the rich only one. The passage also mentions that after the days of sacrifice, the rich should give it in charity alive, but may substitute another. This rule is derived from the books of Bada'i' and applies also to hadaya (gifts).

Key Terms
تتعين (tata'ayyan): Becomes specified or designated for a particular purpose (sacrifice).
نذر (nadhr): Vow; a promise to perform an act of worship. Here, intention alone can constitute a nadhr.
فقير (faqir): Poor person; one who does not own the nisab (minimum wealth) for udhiyah obligation.
غني (ghani): Rich person; one who owns nisab and is obliged to sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Buy another and sacrifice it
C) Give the lost animal in charity
D) Wait for it to be found

Key Takeaway
Intention alone specifies the udhiyah animal absolutely; the rich must replace if lost, the poor need not.

The Hanafi Classification of ‘Itq as a Qurbah, Not ‘Ibadah
Explanation that ‘itq is a qurbah, not an ‘ibadah in origin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that manumission (‘itq) is an act of qurbah, not ‘ibadah, and explain the evidence from its validity from a disbeliever.

Core Idea
‘Itq is a qurbah, not an ‘ibadah — intention is not required for its validity, but it is required for reward.

This passage from a Hanafi usul work establishes a foundational distinction between qurbah (acts of drawing near) and ‘ibadah (acts of worship). The author argues that manumission is not an ‘ibadah by its original legal classification, but a qurbah. The evidence is straightforward: manumission is valid from a disbeliever, yet the worship of a disbeliever is not accepted. Therefore, intention is not a condition for the validity of explicit manumission, though it is required for reward. This ruling has significant practical implications for when a slave becomes free and when the manumitter is rewarded or sinful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
The passage discusses ‘itq (manumission). First, note that the Hanafi school classifies it as a qurbah, not an ‘ibadah. Understand the difference: ‘ibadah requires intention for validity; qurbah does not require intention for validity but does require it for reward.
The Arabic term ‘wad'an’ means 'by original legal classification'.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The author cites the validity of manumission from a disbeliever as proof. Since a disbeliever’s ‘ibadah is invalid, but his manumission is valid, manumission cannot be an ‘ibadah by nature.
The dalil is a text-based proof: 'صحة العتق من الكافر'.
3
Understand the logical deduction
If manumission were an ‘ibadah, it would require intention and belief. Yet it is valid from a disbeliever who lacks both. Therefore, it must be a qurbah, not an ‘ibadah.
This is an implicit qiyas: comparing ‘itq to other qurbat like charity.
4
Apply the classification to explicit and allusive expressions
Because it is a qurbah, explicit (sarih) expressions of manumission are valid without intention. Allusive (kinayah) expressions require intention to determine the act.
The passage later distinguishes between sarih and kinayah.
5
Appreciate the cross-madhhab dispute
Other schools (e.g., Shafi‘i) consider manumission an act of worship requiring intention for validity. The Hanafi evidence from the disbeliever is unique to them, leading to a different practical ruling.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi, explicit ‘itq without intention still frees the slave; in Shafi‘i, it would not.

وَأَمَّا الْعِتْقُ فَعِنْدَنَا لَيْسَ بِعِبَادَةٍ وَضْعَا بِدَلِيْلٍ صِحَّتِهِ مِنَ الْكَافِرِ وَلَا عِبَادَةَ لَهُ فَإِنْ نَوَىٰ وَجْهَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى كَانَ عِبَادَةٌ مُتَاباً عَلَيْهَا وَإِنْ أعْتَقَ بِلَا نِيَّةٍ صَحَ وَلَا ثَوَابَ لَهُ إِنْ كَانَ صَرِيْحاً وَأَمَّا الْكِنَايَاتُ فَلَابُدَّ لَهَا مِنَ النِّيَّةِ فَإِنْ أعْتَقَ لِلصَّنَمِ أَوْلِلشَّيْطَانِ صَحْ وَأَثِمَ وَإِنْ أَعْتَقَ لأَجْلِ مَخْلُوعِ صَحْ وَكَانَ مُبَاحاً لَا ثَوَابَ وَلَا إِثْمَ وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُخَصَّصَ الْإِعْتَاقَ لِلصَّمِ بِمَا إِذَا كَانَ الْمُعْتِقَ كَافِراً أمَّا الْمُسْلِمُ إِذَا اعْتَقَ لَهُ قَاصِداً تَعْظِيْمَهُ كَفَرَ كَمَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يكون الإعتاق لِمَخْلُوعِ مَكْرُوها وَالتَّدْبِيرُ وَالْكِتَابَةُ كَالْعِتْقِ.
ترجمہ: اور رہی آزادی تو وہ وضع کے اعتبار سے ہمارے نزدیک عبادت نہیں ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ کافر کی طرف سے صحیح ہے حالانکہ اسکے لئے عبادت نہیں پس اگر اللہ کی رضا کی نیت کی تو آزادی عبادت ہوگی اسپر ثواب ہوگا اور اگر بدون نیت آزاد کیا تو صحیح ہے اور ثواب نہیں اگر چہ آزادی صریح ہو ۔ اور بہر حال کنایات تو ان کے لئے نبیت ضروری ہے پس اگر بہت کیلئے یا شیطان کیلئے آزاد کیا تو آزادی صحیح ہے اور وہ گناہ گار ہوگا اور اگر کسی مخلوق کیلئے آزاد کیا تو صحیح ہے اور وہ مباح ہے نہ تو اب ہے اور نہ گناہ اور مناسب ہیکہ بت کیلئے آزاد کرنے کو مخصوص کیا جائے جبکہ آزاد کرنے والا کافر ہو ہر حال مسلمان جب بت کیلئے آزاد کرے بت کی تعظیم کے ارادہ سے تو اس نے کفر کیا جب کرد مناسب ہے کسی مخلوق کیلئے آزاد کرنا مکروہ ہوا اور مدبر اور مکاتب بنانا آزاد کرنے کی ہی طرح ہے۔ تشريح العتق في اللغة القوة وفى الشريعة هي قوة حكمية يصير المكلف اهلا للتصرفات الشرعية. آزاد کرنا اصلا عبادت نہیں ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ آزادی کا فر کی طرف سے بھی صحیح ہو جاتی ہے، حالانکہ یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ کافر کی عبادت صحیح نہیں ہوتی اس لئے فقہاء نے کہا ہے آزادی قربت ہے اور قربت کی صحت کے لئے نیت ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ عبادت کی صحت کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے۔ قربت و عبادت میں فرق عبادت نام ہے اس کا جس کے ذریعہ بشرط نیست معبود کو پہچانتے ہوئے عبادت کی جائے اور قربت نام ہے اس عمل کا جسکے ذریعہ متقرب الیہ کو پہچان کر اس کی قربت حاصل کی جائے اس لئے امام رافعی نے اسپر نقل کیا ہے کہ محقق متقربات میں سے ہے۔ جب یہ بات متحقق ہوئی کہ محق منتظر بات میں سے ہے عبادت نہیں ہے تو اس کو عبادت بنانے کے لئے نین ضروری ہے تا کہ عبادت اور عادت میں امتیاز ہو جائے اس پر تفریح پیش کرتے ہوئے علامہ ابن نجیم مصری فرمانے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی مسلمان محض رضاء الہی کی خاطر غلام آزاد کرے گا تو وہ آزاد کرنا عبادت ہو گا اس کو اجر و ثواب ملے گا نوٹی کی ضمیر کا مرجع معتق مسلم ہے کافر کو اگر مرجع قرار دیا تو مسئلہ صحیح نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ کافر بہت غیر معتبر ہے وان اعتقی ۔ اگر کسی نے بدون نبت الفاظ صریحہ سے غلام کو آزاد کر دیا تو غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا اس میں نیت کی ضرورت نہیں لیکن ثواب بدون نیت نہ ملے گا جیسا کہ قاعدہ مشہور ہے لا ثواب الابا لنية. واما الکنایات : الفاظ کنائی کے ذریعہ آزاد کرنے کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے بدون نیت الفاظ کنائی سے غلام کی آزادی کا تحقق نہ ہوگا مثلا لا ملک علیک او خرجت عن ملکی وغیرہ۔ فان اعتق للصنم او للشيطان غلام کو آزاد کرنے کی چند صورتیں ہیں (۱) بت یا شیطان کے چڑھاوے کے لئے غلام آزاد کیا تو آزادی صحیح ؟ البتہ معتق گناہگار ہوگا ۔ آزادی اس لئے صحیح ہے کہ آزادی کا رکن جو رقیت کے ازالہ میں مؤثر ہوتا ہے وہ موجود ؟
As for manumission, according to us it is not an act of worship by nature, evidenced by its validity from a disbeliever, and he has no worship. So if he intends the Face of Allah Almighty, it becomes an act of worship rewarded. And if he manumits without intention, it is valid and he gets no reward if it is explicit. As for kinayat (allusive expressions), intention is necessary for them. So if he manumits for an idol or for Satan, it is valid and he sins. And if he manumits for the sake of a created being, it is valid and permissible, neither reward nor sin. And it is befitting to specify manumission for an idol when the manumitter is a disbeliever. As for a Muslim, if he manumits for it intending its veneration, he disbelieves. Similarly, it is befitting that manumission for a created being is makruh. And tadbir and kitaba are like manumission. Translation: 'As for freedom, by nature it is not an act of worship according to us. The evidence is that it is valid from a disbeliever, although he has no worship. So if he intends the pleasure of Allah, freedom becomes worship and he will get reward. And if he frees without intention, it is valid and there is no reward, even if the freedom is explicit. As for allusive expressions, intention is necessary for them. So if he frees for an idol or for Satan, the freedom is valid and he is sinful. And if he frees for a created being, it is valid and it is permissible, neither reward nor sin. And it is appropriate to specify freeing for an idol when the freeer is a disbeliever. In any case, when a Muslim frees for an idol with the intention of venerating it, he commits disbelief. Similarly, it is appropriate that freeing for a created being is makruh. And making a mudabbar or mukatab is like freeing.' Elucidation: 'Itq linguistically means strength, and in Shariah it is a legal strength by which the accountable person becomes eligible for Shariah transactions. Freeing is not originally an act of worship. The evidence is that freedom is also valid from a disbeliever, although it is agreed that the worship of a disbeliever is not valid. Therefore, the jurists have said that freeing is a qurbah (act of drawing near), and for the validity of a qurbah, intention is not necessary, but for the validity of worship, intention is necessary. The difference between qurbah and worship: worship is the name of that by which, with the condition of negation, one worships the Worshipped while recognizing Him; qurbah is the name of that act by which one seeks nearness to the One sought near, recognizing Him. Therefore, Imam Rafi'i has transmitted that it is from among the assured qurbat. When it is established that it is from among the assured qurbat, not worship, then to make it worship, intention is necessary so that worship and custom may be distinguished. Building on this, 'Allama Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says: If a Muslim frees a slave solely for the pleasure of Allah, then that freeing becomes worship and he will get reward. The pronoun (in 'for it') refers to the Muslim freeer; if it is taken as referring to the disbeliever, the issue would not be correct because the disbeliever's vow is unreliable. And if someone frees a slave with explicit words without intention, the slave becomes free; intention is not needed in that, but reward will not be given without intention, as the famous maxim: 'No reward except with intention.' As for kinayat: With allusive expressions, intention is necessary for freeing; without intention, the slave's freedom does not occur, e.g., 'no ownership over you' or 'you have left my possession' etc. So if he frees for an idol or for Satan: there are several scenarios of freeing a slave. (1) If he frees a slave as an offering for an idol or Satan, the freeing is valid? But the freeer will be sinful. The freeing is valid because the pillar of freeing, which is effective in removing slavery, is present.'
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi ruling on the nature of manumission ('itq). It establishes that 'itq is not an act of worship ('ibadah) by its original legal classification (wad'an), but rather a qurbah (act of drawing near to Allah). The evidence is that 'itq is valid from a disbeliever, whereas worship from a disbeliever is not accepted. Therefore, intention is not a condition for the validity of 'itq when expressed in explicit (sarih) terms; the slave becomes free regardless. However, intention is necessary for reward, and for allusive expressions (kinayat). The passage then discusses various scenarios: manumission for idol or Satan (valid but sinful), for a created being (valid and permissible, though makruh), and emphasizes that a Muslim manumitting for an idol with the intention of veneration commits disbelief. The commentary (Urdu) clarifies the distinction between 'ibadah and qurbah: 'ibadah requires recognition of the worshipped and intention, while qurbah does not require intention for validity but intention is required for it to become an act of worship earning reward. The text quotes Imam Rafi'i and 'Allama Ibn Nujaym to support the classification of 'itq as a qurbah. The passage ends with an enumeration of scenarios of manumission for idols or Satan, noting the validity despite sin.

Key Terms
عتق (‘itq): Legal manumission of a slave; a qurbah that removes slavery.
قربت (qurbah): An act that draws one near to Allah but may be valid without intention.
عبادت (‘ibadah): Worship that requires recognition of the worshipped and intention for validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view expressed in this passage, what is the status of manumission without intention?
A) Invalid because intention is required for all acts.
B) Valid only if the slave is a Muslim.
C) Valid but without reward.
D) Invalid unless done for the sake of Allah.

Key Takeaway
Explicit manumission is valid without intention because it is a qurbah, not an ‘ibadah; intention is needed only for reward.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Intention and Scenarios in Manumission: From Reward to Disbelief
Explanation that ‘itq is a qurbah, not an ‘ibadah in origin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules of intention to different scenarios of manumission and identify when it is valid, sinful, or leads to disbelief.

Core Idea
Explicit manumission is legally valid regardless of intention; the intention determines reward, sin, or disbelief.

Building on the classification of ‘itq as a qurbah, this lesson explores the practical scenarios: explicit vs. allusive expressions, and the diverse intentions that can accompany manumission. The passage shows that while the act itself is valid as long as the pillar (removing slavery) is present, the moral and legal consequences vary enormously — from great reward to sin to even apostasy. Understanding these nuances is essential for a mufti who must issue fatwas on such cases.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish explicit (sarih) from allusive (kinayah)
Explicit words like 'you are free' effect manumission without need for intention. Allusive expressions (e.g., 'I have no need of you') require intention to make them effective.
The passage clearly separates the two with 'فإن كان صريحاً' and 'وأما الكنايات'.
2
Analyze the scenario of manumission for Allah’s sake
If the manumitter intends the Face of Allah, the act becomes an ‘ibadah and he is rewarded. The passage says: 'فإن نوى وجه الله تعالى كان عبادة متاباً عليها'.
The same act becomes worship by intention.
3
Analyze manumission for an idol or Satan
If manumission is for an idol or Satan, it is valid but sinful. Validity is due to the pillar being present; sin is due to the evil intention.
The passage states 'صح وأثم' (valid and he sins).
4
Analyze manumission for a created being
If done for the sake of a created being (e.g., to please a person), it is valid and permissible (mubah), neither reward nor sin. However, the commentary notes it is makruh.
The text says 'لا ثواب ولا إثم' and later 'مكروه'.
5
Understand the extreme case: manumission for an idol by a Muslim
If a Muslim manumits for an idol intending veneration of the idol, he commits disbelief (kufr). This is because it involves shirk.
The passage: 'أما المسلم إذا أعتق له قاصداً تعظيمه كفر'.

وَأَمَّا الْعِتْقُ فَعِنْدَنَا لَيْسَ بِعِبَادَةٍ وَضْعَا بِدَلِيْلٍ صِحَّتِهِ مِنَ الْكَافِرِ وَلَا عِبَادَةَ لَهُ فَإِنْ نَوَىٰ وَجْهَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى كَانَ عِبَادَةٌ مُتَاباً عَلَيْهَا وَإِنْ أعْتَقَ بِلَا نِيَّةٍ صَحَ وَلَا ثَوَابَ لَهُ إِنْ كَانَ صَرِيْحاً وَأَمَّا الْكِنَايَاتُ فَلَابُدَّ لَهَا مِنَ النِّيَّةِ فَإِنْ أعْتَقَ لِلصَّنَمِ أَوْلِلشَّيْطَانِ صَحْ وَأَثِمَ وَإِنْ أَعْتَقَ لأَجْلِ مَخْلُوعِ صَحْ وَكَانَ مُبَاحاً لَا ثَوَابَ وَلَا إِثْمَ وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُخَصَّصَ الْإِعْتَاقَ لِلصَّمِ بِمَا إِذَا كَانَ الْمُعْتِقَ كَافِراً أمَّا الْمُسْلِمُ إِذَا اعْتَقَ لَهُ قَاصِداً تَعْظِيْمَهُ كَفَرَ كَمَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يكون الإعتاق لِمَخْلُوعِ مَكْرُوها وَالتَّدْبِيرُ وَالْكِتَابَةُ كَالْعِتْقِ.

صریحہ سے غلام کو آزاد کر دیا تو غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا اس میں نیت کی ضرورت نہیں لیکن ثواب بدون نیت نہ ملے گا جیسا کہ قاعدہ مشہور ہے لا ثواب الابا لنية. واما الکنایات : الفاظ کنائی کے ذریعہ آزاد کرنے کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے بدون نیت الفاظ کنائی سے غلام کی آزادی کا تحقق نہ ہوگا مثلا لا ملک علیک او خرجت عن ملکی وغیرہ۔ فان اعتق للصنم او للشيطان غلام کو آزاد کرنے کی چند صورتیں ہیں (۱) بت یا شیطان کے چڑھاوے کے لئے غلام آزاد کیا تو آزادی صحیح ؟ البتہ معتق گناہگار ہوگا ۔ آزادی اس لئے صحیح ہے کہ آزادی کا رکن جو رقیت کے ازالہ میں مؤثر ہوتا ہے وہ موجود ؟
As for manumission, according to us it is not an act of worship by nature, evidenced by its validity from a disbeliever, and he has no worship. So if he intends the Face of Allah Almighty, it becomes an act of worship rewarded. And if he manumits without intention, it is valid and he gets no reward if it is explicit. As for kinayat (allusive expressions), intention is necessary for them. So if he manumits for an idol or for Satan, it is valid and he sins. And if he manumits for the sake of a created being, it is valid and permissible, neither reward nor sin. And it is befitting to specify manumission for an idol when the manumitter is a disbeliever. As for a Muslim, if he manumits for it intending its veneration, he disbelieves. Similarly, it is befitting that manumission for a created being is makruh. And tadbir and kitaba are like manumission. Translation: 'As for freedom, by nature it is not an act of worship according to us. The evidence is that it is valid from a disbeliever, although he has no worship. So if he intends the pleasure of Allah, freedom becomes worship and he will get reward. And if he frees without intention, it is valid and there is no reward, even if the freedom is explicit. As for allusive expressions, intention is necessary for them. So if he frees for an idol or for Satan, the freedom is valid and he is sinful. And if he frees for a created being, it is valid and it is permissible, neither reward nor sin. And it is appropriate to specify freeing for an idol when the freeer is a disbeliever. In any case, when a Muslim frees for an idol with the intention of venerating it, he commits disbelief. Similarly, it is appropriate that freeing for a created being is makruh. And making a mudabbar or mukatab is like freeing.' Elucidation: 'Itq linguistically means strength, and in Shariah it is a legal strength by which the accountable person becomes eligible for Shariah transactions. Freeing is not originally an act of worship. The evidence is that freedom is also valid from a disbeliever, although it is agreed that the worship of a disbeliever is not valid. Therefore, the jurists have said that freeing is a qurbah (act of drawing near), and for the validity of a qurbah, intention is not necessary, but for the validity of worship, intention is necessary. The difference between qurbah and worship: worship is the name of that by which, with the condition of negation, one worships the Worshipped while recognizing Him; qurbah is the name of that act by which one seeks nearness to the One sought near, recognizing Him. Therefore, Imam Rafi'i has transmitted that it is from among the assured qurbat. When it is established that it is from among the assured qurbat, not worship, then to make it worship, intention is necessary so that worship and custom may be distinguished. Building on this, 'Allama Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says: If a Muslim frees a slave solely for the pleasure of Allah, then that freeing becomes worship and he will get reward. The pronoun (in 'for it') refers to the Muslim freeer; if it is taken as referring to the disbeliever, the issue would not be correct because the disbeliever's vow is unreliable. And if someone frees a slave with explicit words without intention, the slave becomes free; intention is not needed in that, but reward will not be given without intention, as the famous maxim: 'No reward except with intention.' As for kinayat: With allusive expressions, intention is necessary for freeing; without intention, the slave's freedom does not occur, e.g., 'no ownership over you' or 'you have left my possession' etc. So if he frees for an idol or for Satan: there are several scenarios of freeing a slave. (1) If he frees a slave as an offering for an idol or Satan, the freeing is valid? But the freeer will be sinful. The freeing is valid because the pillar of freeing, which is effective in removing slavery, is present.'
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi ruling on the nature of manumission ('itq). It establishes that 'itq is not an act of worship ('ibadah) by its original legal classification (wad'an), but rather a qurbah (act of drawing near to Allah). The evidence is that 'itq is valid from a disbeliever, whereas worship from a disbeliever is not accepted. Therefore, intention is not a condition for the validity of 'itq when expressed in explicit (sarih) terms; the slave becomes free regardless. However, intention is necessary for reward, and for allusive expressions (kinayat). The passage then discusses various scenarios: manumission for idol or Satan (valid but sinful), for a created being (valid and permissible, though makruh), and emphasizes that a Muslim manumitting for an idol with the intention of veneration commits disbelief. The commentary (Urdu) clarifies the distinction between 'ibadah and qurbah: 'ibadah requires recognition of the worshipped and intention, while qurbah does not require intention for validity but intention is required for it to become an act of worship earning reward. The text quotes Imam Rafi'i and 'Allama Ibn Nujaym to support the classification of 'itq as a qurbah. The passage ends with an enumeration of scenarios of manumission for idols or Satan, noting the validity despite sin.

Key Terms
صريح (sarih): Explicit words that clearly indicate manumission without need for intention.
كناية (kinayah): Allusive words that require intention to effect manumission.
تدبير (tadbir): Declaring that a slave will be free upon the owner's death.
كتابة (kitabah): A contract where a slave buys his freedom in installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Muslim says to his slave 'You are free' intending to free him as an offering to an idol but without intending veneration of the idol. According to the passage, what is the ruling?
A) The manumission is invalid because it is for an idol.
B) The manumission is valid but the Muslim disbelieves.
C) The manumission is valid and the Muslim sins.
D) The manumission is valid and the Muslim does not sin.

Key Takeaway
Intention in manumission determines reward, sin, or disbelief, but explicit words always make the slave free.

Definitions of Tadbir and Kitabah
Definitions of tadbir and kitabah with brief effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tadbir and kitabah, distinguish them as forms of emancipation, and apply these definitions in constructing a fatwa.

Core Idea
Tadbir is freedom after death; kitabah is freedom by payment — two distinct emancipation contracts.

This lesson introduces two key terms from the chapter on emancipation (itq) in Hanafi fiqh. Tadbir and kitabah are both valid contracts that change the legal status of a slave, but they differ in timing and condition. Understanding these definitions is essential for a mufti when advising on slave-related matters (though now historical, the principles apply to analogous contracts).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its parties
Read each definition and note who is speaking (master) and who is receiving the declaration (slave). Tadbir involves a declaration by the master; kitabah involves a command to pay a consideration.
2
Parse the operative phrase
In tadbir, the key phrase is 'You are free after my death.' In kitabah, it is 'I command you to pay a consideration for freedom.' Identify the conditional element in tadbir (death) and the obligation element in kitabah (payment).
3
Note the resulting legal status
After the declaration, the slave is called mudabbar (for tadbir) or mukatab (for kitabah). These statuses confer specific rights and restrictions: a mudabbar cannot be sold, and a mukatab can acquire property.
4
Understand the effect after completion
After the master's death (tadbir) or after full payment (kitabah), the slave becomes free. The text notes that after freedom, certain transactions that were valid during slavery become prohibited, similar for both.
The exact wording in the passage about prohibited transactions is partially unclear due to OCR, but the principle is that emancipation removes the slave's capacity to be a party to certain contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتدبير والكتابة: اگر آقا اپنے غلام سے یوں کہ دے کہ میرے مرنے کے بعد تو آزاد ہے تو اس غلام کو مدبر کہا جائے گا اور آقا کے مرنے کے بعد وہ غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ مکاتب جس کو آقا بدل کتابت ادا کرنے کا حکم دیدے اس کو مکاتب کہتے ہیں۔ لہذا آزادی کے بعد جس طرح اس کے ساتھ وہ تمام تصرفات ممنوع ہو جاتے ہیں جو اس کے غلام کے ہوتے ہوئے درست تھے نہیں علم تو یہ اور کتابت کا بھی ہے۔
And tadbir and kitabah: If the master says to his slave, 'You are free after my death,' then that slave is called mudabbar, and after the master's death, that slave becomes free. A mukatab is one whom the master commands to pay a consideration (badal kitabah) [for freedom]; he is called mukatab. Therefore, after freedom, just as all those transactions that were valid while he was a slave become prohibited, [there is something similar] and this also applies to kitabah.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage defines two types of emancipation in Hanafi fiqh. Tadbir is when the master declares that the slave will be free after his death; such a slave is called mudabbar. The emancipation takes effect upon the master's death and is irrevocable. Kitabah is a contract where the master agrees to free the slave upon payment of a specified sum; the slave is called mukatab. The text then notes that after emancipation, prohibitions on transactions that were valid during slavery apply similarly, though the final part is unclear due to OCR corruption. These terms are important in the chapter on emancipation (itq).

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbīr): A declaration by the master that a slave will be free after the master's death.
کتابت (kitābah): A contract between master and slave whereby the slave earns freedom by paying a fixed sum in installments.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave for whom tadbir has been declared; he will be free after the master's death.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract; he is working toward freedom by paying installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what distinguishes tadbir from kitabah?
A) Tadbir requires payment; kitabah does not.
B) Tadbir takes effect after the master's death; kitabah takes effect after payment.
C) Tadbir is revocable; kitabah is not.
D) Tadbir applies only to male slaves; kitabah only to female.

Key Takeaway
Tadbir and kitabah are two distinct emancipation contracts: one contingent on death, the other on payment.

Intention in Wasiat, Waqf, and Nikah: Validity vs Reward
Ruling with proof and definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between validity and reward in wasiat, waqf, and nikah, and state when niyyah is required for each.

Core Idea
Acts like wasiat, waqf, and nikah are valid without intention of worship, but reward depends on that intention.

This passage addresses a common question: do contracts like wills, endowments, and marriage require an intention of worship (niyyah al-qurbah) to be valid? The Hanafi answer is nuanced: validity and reward are separate. A Muslim who performs these acts without explicit intention still performs a valid legal act, but only receives divine reward if he intended closeness to Allah. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the practical implications for a mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three acts and their default status
List wasiat, waqf, and nikah. Note that the author treats them as legal acts that are not inherently acts of worship. The default rule: validity does not require niyyah al-qurbah.
Waqf is explicitly stated as not worship because it is valid from a kafir.
2
Understand the proof for each act's non-ibadah status
For wasiat: analogous to emancipation (itq) – valid without qurbah. For waqf: validity from a kafir proves it is not worship. For nikah: it is closer to worship but still valid without intention, though intention is needed for reward.
The proof for waqf is a powerful usul argument: acts of worship are not valid from a kafir.
3
Analyze the Hanafi ikhtilaf on waqf definition
Abu Hanifa defines waqf as retaining ownership with charity of usufruct (revocable). Sahibayn define it as confinement of the asset from ownership (irrevocable). This affects the role of intention.
The mufta bihi is the view of Sahibayn: waqf is irrevocable and the asset passes to Allah.
4
Apply the principle to nikah
Nikah is a confirmed sunnah, closer to worship. Intention is required for reward: to preserve chastity and have children. But the contract is valid even without that intention.
The text cites i'tidal (moderation) – neither excess nor neglect of worship.
5
Synthesize for fatwa practice
When a mufti receives a case about these acts, he must rule on validity first (always valid if conditions met), then advise on reward separately. The mufti should encourage niyyah al-qurbah but not invalidate the act if absent.
This distinction prevents hardship: people may perform these acts without explicit worship intention, yet they are legally binding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْوَصِيَّةُ فَكا العتق إن فَصَدَ التَّقَرُّبَ فَلَهُ الثَّوَابُ وَإِلَّا فَهيَ صَحِيحَة فَقَط وَأَمَّا الْوَقْفُ فَلَيْسَ بِعِبَادَةِ وَضْعاً بِدَلِيْلِ صِحْتِهِ مِنَ الْكَافِرِ فَإِنْ نَوَى الْقُرْبَةَ فَلَهُ الثَّوَابُ وَإِلَّا فَلَا. وأما الوقف الوقف في اللغة الحبس وفي الشريعة حبس العين على ملك الواقف والتصدق بالمنفعة عند ابي حنيفة فيجوز رجوعه وعندهما حبس العين عن التمليك مع التصدق بمنفعتها فتكون العين زائلة الى ملك الله تعالى من وجه. وقف فی نفسہ عبادت نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر یہ عبادت ہوتا تب کا فر کی طرف سے صحیح نہیں ہوتا جب وقف فی قصہ عبادت نہیں رہا تو اگر کوئی مسلمان وقف کرتے وقت قربت کی نیت کرے گا تبھی اسے ثواب ملے گا ورنہ نہیں اگرچہ وقف بدون نیت بھی کیسی ہو جاتا ہے۔ وَأَمَّا النِّكَاحُ فَقَالُوا إِنَّهَا أَقْرَبُ إِلَى الْعِبَادَاتِ حَتَّى أَنَّ الْإِشْتِغَالَ بِهِ أَفْضَلُ مِنَ التَّعَلَى لمَحْضِ الْعِبَادَةِ وَهُوَ عِندَ الْإِعْتِدَالِ سُنَّةٌ مُؤكَّدَةً عَلَى الصَّحِيحِ فَيَحْتَاجُ إِلَى النِّيَّةِ لِتَحْصِيل الثَّوَابِ وَهُوَ أَنْ يَقْصِدَ إعْفَافَ نَفْسِهِ وَتَحْصِيْنَهَا وَحُصُوْلَ وَلَدٍ وَفَسَّرْنَا الْإِعْتَدَالَ فِي الشَّرْحِ الْكَبِيرِ شَرْحِ الْكَنْزِ
As for wasiat, it is like emancipation: if he intends closeness (taqarrub), he has reward; otherwise it is only valid. As for waqf, it is not a worship in origin, evidenced by its validity from a kafir; if he intends qurbah, he has reward; otherwise not. ... Waqf linguistically is confinement; legally, according to Abu Hanifa, it is the confinement of the asset in the ownership of the waqif and giving charity of the usufruct, so he may revoke it; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is the confinement of the asset from ownership and giving charity of its usufruct, so the asset passes to the ownership of Allah in a sense. Waqf in itself is not worship, because if it were worship, it would not be valid from a kafir. So if a Muslim intends qurbah at the time of waqf, he gets reward; otherwise not, although the waqf becomes valid without intention. As for nikah, they said it is closer to acts of worship, such that engaging in it is better than devoting to mere worship. It is a confirmed sunnah at i'tidal (moderation) according to the correct view, so it needs intention for attaining reward. He should intend to keep himself chaste and protect oneself, and to have children. And we have explained i'tidal in the Sharh al-Kabir of Kanz (al-Daqa'iq).
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage covers three acts: wasiat (will), waqf (endowment), and nikah (marriage). For each, it distinguishes between validity and reward. Wasiat is like emancipation: valid even without intention of qurbah, but reward requires that intention. Waqf is not inherently a worship; proof is that it is valid from a kafir. So if a Muslim intends qurbah, he gets reward; otherwise the waqf is valid but rewardless. The text also defines waqf according to the Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa sees it as retaining ownership with charity of usufruct (revocable), while the Sahibayn see it as transfer of ownership to Allah (irrevocable). Nikah is closer to worship; it is a confirmed sunnah at i'tidal (neither excess nor neglect). Intention is needed for reward: to preserve chastity, protect oneself, and have children. This passage illustrates the Hanafi principle that many acts are valid without intention for qurbah, but reward depends on that intention.

Key Terms
وصية (waṣiyyah): A transfer of ownership (tamlik) suspended after death, valid up to one-third of the estate.
وقف (waqf): Linguistically: confinement. Legally: confinement of an asset from ownership (according to Sahibayn) or retaining ownership with charity of usufruct (according to Abu Hanifa).
نکاح (nikāḥ): Marriage; a contract that is closer to worship; a confirmed sunnah at i'tidal.
قربة (qurbah): Closeness to Allah; intention to seek divine reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What evidence does the passage provide to prove that waqf is not an act of worship in itself?
A) It is valid from a Muslim without intention.
B) It is valid from a non-Muslim (kafir).
C) Abu Hanifa allows revocation.
D) It involves property transfer.

Key Takeaway
Validity of wasiat, waqf, and nikah does not require intention of worship; reward does. The mufta bihi for waqf is Sahibayn's view (irrevocable).

Nikah: Definition, Superiority, and Five Legal Rulings
Definition, superiority arguments, and fivefold legal classification of nikah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi fivefold classification of nikah (fard, wajib, sunnah muakkadah, makruh, mubah/haram) to individual cases and construct a fatwa by evaluating the inquirer's ability, fear, and intention.

Core Idea
Marriage in Hanafi fiqh is closer to worship and can be obligatory, necessary, or disliked depending on one’s ability, fear of sin, and intention.

This passage from Sharh al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair lays the foundation for a mufti's assessment of marriage. It defines nikah, establishes its superiority over solitary worship, and provides a fivefold classification that turns on individual circumstances. As a mufti, you must evaluate each case's unique factors—ability, fear, intention—before issuing a ruling. This lesson will walk you through the arguments and the classification so you can apply them in fatwa-giving.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its definition
Understand the legal definition of nikah as a contract transferring ownership of benefit of intercourse, and that it is considered closer to worship.
2
Evaluate the superiority arguments
Examine the four proofs from al-Bada'i showing marriage is superior to solitary worship, and the response to the objection of Jesus.
3
Assess the individual's situation
Determine whether the person has ability to pay mahr and maintenance, and whether there is fear of falling into zina or other prohibited acts.
4
Apply the fivefold classification
Match the situation to the correct ruling: fard, wajib, sunnah muakkadah, makruh, or mubah/haram (implied).
5
Issue the fatwa with intention condition
Remind that intention to seek reward is necessary for the act to be worship; advise accordingly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا النِّكَاحُ فَقَالُوا إِنَّهَا أَقْرَبُ إِلَى الْعِبَادَاتِ حَتَّى أَنَّ الْإِشْتِغَالَ بِهِ أَفْضَلُ مِنَ التَّعَلَى لمَحْضِ الْعِبَادَةِ وَهُوَ عِندَ الْإِعْتِدَالِ سُنَّةٌ مُؤكَّدَةً عَلَى الصَّحِيحِ فَيَحْتَاجُ إِلَى النِّيَّةِ لِتَحْصِيل الثَّوَابِ وَهُوَ أَنْ يَقْصِدَ إعْفَافَ نَفْسِهِ وَتَحْصِيْنَهَا وَحُصُوْلَ وَلَدٍ وَفَسَّرْنَا الْإِعْتَدَالَ فِي الشَّرْحِ الْكَبِيرِ شَرْحِ الْكَنْزِ
ترجمہ : اور رہا نکاح تو انہوں نے کہا کہ وہ عبادات کے بہت قریب ہے حتی کہ اس میں مشغول ہونا محض عبادت کے لئے تخلیہ سے بہتر ہے اور وہ حالت اعتدال میں سنت موکدہ ہے صحیح قول کے بموجب چنا نچہ تحصیل ثواب کے لئے نیت کی ضرورت پیش آئیگی اور وہ یہ کہ ارادہ کرے اپنے نفس کی عفت اور اس کی پاکدامنی کا اور اولاد حاصل کرنے کا اور کنز کی شرح شرح کبیر میں ہم نے اعتدال کی تفسیر کر دی ہے۔
تشريح النكاح هو فى اللغة الضم والجمع و فى الشريعة هو عقد يرد على تمليك منفعة البضع قصداً والمراد بالنكاح هنا الوطى المترتب على العقد الصحيح. نکاح من جد عبادت ہے اور من وجہ معاملہ ہے لیکن عبادت کے زیادہ قریب ہے چونکہ مسلموں کی کثرت کا باعث ہونے کے ساتھ ساتھ سبب عفت اور پاکدامنی کا ذریعہ بھی ہے۔ حتى ان الاشتغال به: ازدواجی زندگی میں مشغول رہ کر زندگی گذار نا خلوت میں رہ کر عبادت کرنے کے مقابلہ میں کئی اعتبار سے بڑھا ہوا اور بہتر ہے جیسا کہ صاحب بدائع نے چند طرق سے استدلال کیا ہے۔ (1) نکاح کرنا سنت ہے جبکہ محض عبادت کے لئے خلوت اختیار کرنا نفل ہے اور سنت نفل سے بڑھکر ہے۔ (۲) ترک سنت پر وعید ہے اور ترک نفل پر وعید نہیں۔
(۳) آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے نکاح کئے اور اس پر مواظبت فرمائی اور آپ نے نکاح سے تخلیہ نہیں فرمایا بلکہ دوسروں کے مقابلہ میں اور زیادہ نکاح کئے ، جب آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے حق میں نکاح کی افضلیت ثابت ہوگئی تو آپ کی امت کے حق میں بھی یہی افضل ہوگا اس لئے کہ اصل شرائع میں عموم ہے اور خصوص دلیل پر موقوف ہے۔ (۴) یہ نکاح نوافل سے افضل ہے کیونکہ اولاد کے حصول کا سبب ہے اپنے نفس کو بے حیائی اور اپنی بیوی کو نفقہ، سکتی اور لباس دیکر بے حیائی سے بچانا ہے۔ ان امور مذکورہ کی وجہ سے نکاح کو نفلی عبادت کے لئے خلوت اختیار کرنے پر افضلیت حاصل ہے۔ اور حضرت کئی علیہ السلام کی ترک نکاح پر جو تعریف قرآن شریف میں مذکور ہے تو وہ ان کی شریعت کے اعتبار سے ہے ہماری شریعت میں یہ افضلیت کا باعث نہیں ہے۔ (حاشيه الحموي مع الاشباه ص ۸۳)
وهو عند الاعتدال سنة مؤكدة : نكاح کی حکم کے اعتبار سے پانچ قسمیں ہیں۔ (۱) فرض : جبکہ زنا میں مبتلا ہونے کا کامل اور پختہ یقین ہو اور یہ یقین ہو کہ نکاح کے ذریعہ ہی وہ زنا سے محفوظ رہ سکتا ہے تو فرض ہے۔ (۲) واجب ہے جبکہ زنا میں پڑ جانے کا خوف تو نہ ہو لیکن نفس کو بد نظری یا استمنا بالکلف سے بچانا ممکن نہ ہو ۔ (۳) سنت مؤکدہ ہے جبکہ نائح وطی ، مہر اور بیوی کے نفقہ پر بھی قادر ہو اس طرح کہ فرض کے ترک سنتوں سے اعراض اور ظلم میں پڑ جانے کا اندیشہ نہ ہو۔ اگر ان میں سے کسی ایک پر بھی نالح قادر نہ ہو تو صاحب بحر کی تصریح کے مطابق اس کے حق میں نکاح سنت مؤکدہ نہ ہوگا۔ (۴) مکروہ ہے جبکہ علم میں پڑ جانے کا خوف ہو۔ (۵) جب علم میں
As for marriage, they said it is closer to worship, such that engaging in it is superior to seclusion for mere worship. And it is, in the state of moderation, a confirmed sunnah according to the correct view. Thus it needs intention for attaining reward, and that is that one intends to keep himself chaste and to obtain offspring. We have explained moderation in al-Sharh al-Kabir, the commentary on al-Kanz. ... Tashrih al-nikah: linguistically it means joining and gathering; in Shariah it is a contract that effects the ownership of the benefit of sexual intercourse intentionally, and by nikah here is meant the sexual intercourse resulting from the valid contract. Marriage is from one aspect worship and from another aspect transaction, but it is closer to worship because it causes increase of Muslims and is a means of chastity and purity. Even that engagement in it is superior in several respects to remaining in seclusion for worship, as the author of al-Bada'i has argued in several ways: (1) Marriage is sunnah while seclusion for worship is nafl, and sunnah is superior to nafl. (2) There is a threat for abandoning sunnah, not for abandoning nafl. (3) The Prophet (peace be upon him) married and persisted in it, and did not abandon marriage; rather he married more than others. Since the superiority of marriage for the Prophet is proven, the same applies to his ummah because the original in laws is generality and specificity depends on evidence. (4) It is superior to nawafil because it is a means of obtaining children, protecting oneself from immorality, and protecting one's wife from immorality by providing maintenance, shelter, and clothing. For these reasons, marriage is superior to seclusion for nafl worship. As for the praise of Jesus (peace be upon him) for abandoning marriage mentioned in the Quran, that is according to his law; in our law it is not a cause of superiority. (Margin of al-Hamawi with al-Ashbah, p. 83) And it is, in the state of moderation, a confirmed sunnah: the rulings of nikah are five types: (1) Fard: when one has certain conviction of falling into zina and believes that only marriage can protect him. (2) Wajib: when there is no fear of zina but one cannot avoid casting looks or masturbation by effort. (3) Confirmed sunnah: when one is able to pay dower and wife's maintenance, and there is no fear of failing in obligatory duties or injustice. If unable to any of these, then according to al-Bahr, it is not confirmed sunnah for him. (4) Makruh: when there is fear of injustice. (5) When [cut off].
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed Hanafi analysis of marriage (nikah). It begins by establishing that nikah is closer to worship than to transaction, such that engaging in it is superior to solitary worship. The reason is that marriage preserves chastity, increases the Muslim community, and is a means to obtain righteous offspring. The text then cites four arguments from al-Bada'i to demonstrate the superiority of marriage over seclusion for nafl worship. It also addresses the objection that Jesus (peace be upon him) praised celibacy, clarifying that this applies to his shariah, not ours. Finally, the passage presents the fivefold classification of the ruling of nikah according to individual circumstances: fard (obligatory) when zina is certain; wajib (necessary) when one fears falling into forbidden acts but not zina; sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah) when one can fulfill marital responsibilities; makruh (disliked) when there is fear of injustice; and a fifth category that is not completed in the text (likely mubah or haram depending on context). This classification is a practical tool for muftis: they must assess the individual's situation before issuing a ruling on the desirability or necessity of marriage.

Key Terms
النكاح (al-nikah): A contract that effects ownership of the benefit of sexual intercourse, or the sexual intercourse resulting from a valid contract.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah muakkadah): A confirmed recommended act; its abandonment is disliked but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does nikah become fard (obligatory) according to the passage?
A) When one can afford the mahr and maintenance
B) When one fears falling into zina and believes only marriage can prevent it
C) When one desires offspring
D) When one's family pressures him to marry

Key Takeaway
The ruling of nikah varies from fard to makruh based on personal circumstances; a mufti must assess each case individually before issuing a fatwa.

Validity of Marriage in Jest and with Unfamiliar Words
Ruling that marriage is valid even if done in jest, with exceptions for unfamiliar words

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that marriage in jest is valid, identify the relied-upon position on marriage with unfamiliar words, and apply the hadith proof to similar contracts.

Core Idea
Marriage in jest is binding; intention is irrelevant. Unfamiliar words: fatwa upholds validity.

This passage tackles two practical scenarios a mufti may face: a marriage contract made jokingly, and a contract using words the parties do not understand. The Hanafi school gives weight to external expression over internal intention in marriage, divorce, and return, as confirmed by a prophetic hadith. For unfamiliar words, although there is a disagreement, the operative fatwa confirms validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on marriage in jest
Determine the hukm: the passage explicitly states that marriage is valid even if done in jest, because intention (niyyah) is not a condition for its validity.
Contrast with acts of worship where intention is essential.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Find the hadith from Abu Hurairah (ra) that three matters are effective whether done seriously or in jest: marriage, divorce, and return. This is a dalil naqli.
The hadith is quoted in the explanation section of the passage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling: the word 'jidd' (serious) and 'hazl' (jest) are both effective, meaning the legal consequences follow regardless of intent. Thus, marriage in jest is valid.
The hadith is general and covers all three matters equally.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on unfamiliar words
If a contract is made with a word whose meaning is unknown to the parties, there is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars. Some may consider it invalid due to lack of proper consent.
The ikhtilaf is recorded, but the passage does not detail the opposing arguments.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The passage states that the fatwa is on its validity, even if witnesses do not understand the words, as per al-Bazzaziyyah. This is the relied-upon position for muftis.
The authority level is fatawa mutakhkhirin, from the text al-Bazzaziyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما تكن النية فيه شرط صحته قالوا يصح النكاح مع الهزل لكن قالوا لو عقد بلفظ لا يعرف معناه ففيه خلاف والفتوى على صحته علم الشهود أو لا كما في البزازية. ترجمه: اور جبکہ نکاح میں نیت اس کے صحیح ہونے کی شرط نہیں ہے فقہاء نے کہا کہ نکاح مذاق کے ساتھ درست ہے لیکن انہوں نے کہا کہ اگر ایسے لفظ سے عقد کیا جس کے معنی معلوم نہ ہو تو اس میں اختلاف ہے اور فتویٰ ان کی صحت پر ہے گواہوں کو معلوم ہو یا نہ ہو جیسا کہ بزازیہ میں ہے۔ تشریح جبکہ آپ کو یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ نکاح کی صحت کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں ہے تو فقہاء کرام فرماتے ہیں کہ مذاق میں بھی نکاح صحیح ہوتا ہے بشرطیکہ شرائط نکاح پائے جائیں اور کوئی مانع بھی نہ ہو کیونکہ نکاح میں نیت کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ اعتبار کلام کا ہو گا۔ نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا : عن ابي هريرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ثلاث جدهن جد وهزلهن جد النكاح والطلاق والرجعة. ولو عقد بلفظ لا يعرف معنى ففيه خلاف والفتوى على صحته.
And since intention is not a condition for its validity, they said that marriage is valid even with jest. But they said that if he contracts with a word whose meaning is not known, then there is a dispute, and the fatwa is on its validity, whether the witnesses know it or not, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. Translation: And since intention is not a condition for the validity of marriage, the jurists said that marriage with jest is valid. But they said that if a contract is made with a word whose meaning is not known, then there is disagreement, and the fatwa is on its validity, whether the witnesses know or not, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. Explanation: When you have understood that intention is not a condition for the validity of marriage, the noble jurists say that marriage is valid even in jest, provided the conditions of marriage are present and there is no impediment, because intention is not considered in marriage; rather, the speech is considered. The Prophet ﷺ said, from Abu Hurairah: 'Three matters are serious and jest alike: marriage, divorce, and return.' And if he contracts with a word whose meaning is not known, then there is disagreement, and the fatwa is on its validity.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage addresses a key principle in Hanafi marriage law: intention is not a condition for the validity of the contract. Therefore, if someone performs the marriage contract in jest, without actually intending to get married, the contract is still legally binding. The author cites the well-known hadith from Abu Hurairah that three matters are effective whether done seriously or in jest: marriage, divorce, and return (raj'ah). This underscores the seriousness of these affairs. However, if the words used in the contract are not understood by the parties (e.g., using a foreign language that neither party comprehends), there is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars. The relied-upon position (fatwa) is that the marriage is still valid, even if the witnesses do not understand the words, as recorded in al-Bazzaziyyah. This ruling stems from the principle that in contracts of marriage, the external expression (kalam) is given weight over internal intention, except in cases of clear misunderstanding or lack of consent.

Key Terms
هزل (hazl): Jest or play; performing an action without intending its legal consequences.
لفظ لا يعرف معناه (lafz la yu'raf ma'anah): A word whose meaning is not known by the parties contracting; there is a dispute about the validity of such a marriage, but the fatwa is that it is valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a marriage contract performed in jest?
A) It is invalid because intention is missing.
B) It is valid provided the witnesses understand the words.
C) It is valid because intention is not a condition for marriage.
D) It is invalid unless the person later confirms it.

Key Takeaway
Marriage in jest is valid and binding; the fatwa also upholds validity when unfamiliar words are used, emphasizing the primacy of external expression in marriage contracts.

Talaq and Itq: Occur Without Intention and Under Compulsion
Contrasting talaq/itq with hiba regarding intention and consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that talaq and itq occur without intention and under compulsion, and distinguish between qada' and diyanah in such cases.

Core Idea
Talaq and itq are unique: they take effect even without intention and under compulsion, unlike other transactions.

In this lesson, we examine a distinctive Hanafi rule: divorce (talaq) and manumission (itq) occur regardless of intention or consent. Unlike gifts (hiba) or sales, which require willing consent, talaq and itq are acts that cannot be annulled, and thus they take effect even if the person is inattentive, forgetful, or coerced. The passage also clarifies the difference between judicial ruling (qada') and inner religious reality (diyanah), and addresses a specific issue of written divorce under compulsion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
Recognize that talaq and itq are contrasted with hiba and sale: they do not require intention or consent for occurrence.
This is the central principle derived from the source.
2
Distinguish annullable vs non-annullable acts
Understand Imam Abu Hanifa's principle: acts that can be annulled (like sale) are ineffective under compulsion; acts that cannot be annulled (like talaq, itq) are effective.
The key distinction is the nature of the act, not the presence of coercion.
3
Apply the rule to a coerced person
If a person is compelled to utter divorce words, talaq occurs because consent is not a condition.
Contrast with Shafi'i school which invalidates such divorce.
4
Differentiate qada' and diyanah
For someone who does not understand Arabic divorce words, the court (qada') rules talaq based on apparent words, but religiously (diyanah) it may not be valid if there was no intent.
Some mashayikh say neither qada' nor diyanah is effective.
5
Apply to written divorce under compulsion
Writing divorce under compulsion: according to Fatawa Qadikhan, it does not occur because writing substitutes speech only out of necessity, and compulsion does not create necessity.
Shows that the rule has nuances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

صحیح اور درست نہ ہوگا لعدم الرضاء بخلاف الطلاق والے مسئلہ میں اگر کسی کو عربی زبان میں طلاق و عتاق ، تدبیر وغیر کی تلقین کی دو ان کے معنی نہیں جانتا ہے اور اس نے ان الفاظ کو ادا کر دیا تو مصنف علیہ الرحمہ نے علی الاطلاق ان کے وقوع کا حکم لگایا ہے جبکہ فقیہ ابدالی فرماتے ہیں کہ قضاء تو طلاق وعتاق وغیرہ کا متفق ہو جائے گا لیکن دیا یہ نہیں اس لئے کہ جب وہ ان کے معنی مطلب ہی کو نہیں جانتا تو اس کا فَصَرِيحٌ وَكِتَايَةٌ وَالْأَوَّلُ لَا يَحْتَاجُ فِي وَقَوْعِهِ إِلَيْهَا فَلَوْ طَلَّقَ غَافِلًا أَوْ سَاهِياً أَوْ مُخْطِي وَقَعَ قَالُوا إِنَّ الطَّلَاقَ يَقَعُ بِالْأَلْفَاظِ الْمُصْحَفَةِ قَضَاءً وَلكِنْ لَا بُدَّ أنْ يَقْصِدَهَا بِاللَّفْظِ. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال طلاق تو وہ صریح اور کنایہ ہے پس اول اپنے وقوع میں اس کی محتاج نہیں ہے پس اگر غفلت میں یا بھول کر یا غلطی سے طلاق دیدی تو واقع ہو جائے گی اور فقہاء کہتے ہیں کہ طلاق الفاظ مصحفہ سے قضاء واقع ہو جاتی ہے لیکن لفظ سے اس کا ارادہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ تشريح الطلاق وهو لغة رفع القيد سواء كان حسنا كقيد الفرس وقيد الاسير او معنوياً كقيد النكاح وهو الارتباط الحاصل بين الزوجين ( فتاوى النوازل ص (۱۹۶) وشرعاً رفع قيد النكاح في الحال او المآل بلفظ مخصوص . (شای ج ۳۳۰۴۱) جن الفاظ سے طلاق دی جاتی ہے ان کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) صریح (۲) کنایہ۔ الفاظ صریح سے طلاق دیتے وقت نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور طلاق بدون نیت بھی قضاء واقع ہو جائیگی البتہ
Contrary to divorce and manumission: If someone prompted the words of divorce and manumission, and the one prompted does not understand their meaning and import, and he utters the words of divorce and manumission due to someone's prompting, then divorce and manumission will occur, because for their occurrence consent is not a condition. Therefore if someone was compelled: When you know that for occurrence of divorce and manumission consent is not a condition, if someone forcibly extracted the words of divorce and manumission from another's tongue, then divorce and manumission will occur, while the three Imams do not believe in the occurrence of divorce of the coerced person. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the principle is that acts of the coerced person that can be annulled (Faskh) are not effective, like marriage, sale, etc., and those acts that cannot be annulled, like divorce and manumission, become effective even from a coerced person. Contrary to sale and purchase, in which consent is necessary; if sale and purchase were done by force and coercion, that sale and purchase will not be valid due to lack of consent. Contrary to the issue of divorce: If someone prompted a person with Arabic words of divorce, manumission, tadbir, etc., and he does not know their meaning, and he uttered these words, the author (may Allah have mercy on him) ruled unconditionally that they occur. While Faqih Abadali says that in terms of judicial ruling (qada'), divorce and manumission etc. will definitely occur, but not in terms of inner religious reality (diyanah), because when he does not know their meaning at all, his intent and will are not found, so in diyanah the ruling of occurrence of divorce and manumission will not be given. But the judicial ruling is based on the apparent, and apparently these words indicate the occurrence of divorce and manumission, and their meanings are well-known, therefore they will be interpreted according to their apparent meaning even if intent and will are not found. Some mashayikh and a group say that in the mentioned scenario, neither qada' nor diyanah ruling will follow. Issue: If someone was compelled to write divorce regarding his wife and he wrote it, then in Fatawa Qadikhan it is stated that divorce will not occur, and the reason given is that writing stands in place of speech out of necessity, and here there is no necessity. As for divorce, it is either explicit (sarih) or implicit (kinayah). The first does not need intention for its occurrence. So if one divorces inattentively, forgetfully, or mistakenly, it occurs. They said that divorce occurs with musahhaf (mispronounced) words in terms of qada', but one must intend them with the word. Translation: And in any case, divorce is explicit and implicit; the first does not need intention for its occurrence. So if one divorces inattentively, forgetfully, or mistakenly, it occurs. And the jurists say that divorce occurs with musahhaf words in qada', but it is necessary to intend them with the word. Explanation of divorce: Linguistically, it means removal of a restraint, whether physical like the restraints of a horse or a prisoner, or conceptual like the restraint of marriage, i.e., the connection between spouses (Fatawa al-Nawazil, p. 196). Legally, it is the removal of the restraint of marriage immediately or eventually with a specific word (Shami, vol. 3, p. 3041). The words by which divorce is given are of two types: (1) explicit (sarih), (2) implicit (kinayah). When giving divorce with explicit words, intention is not required, and divorce without intention occurs in qada'.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the Hanafi ruling regarding talaq (divorce) and itq (manumission) in contrast to hiba. The key point is that talaq and itq do not require intention or consent for their occurrence. Therefore, they take effect even if the person is inattentive, forgetful, mistaken, or acting under compulsion. This is based on a fundamental difference in legal philosophy: talaq and itq are acts that nullify a contract (marriage or slavery) and cannot be reversed (they are not qabil al-faskh), so the element of free will is not a condition for their validity. The text also distinguishes between qada' (judicial ruling) and diyanah (inner religious reality). For a person who does not understand the meaning of Arabic divorce words and merely repeats them, the court will consider it a valid divorce because the apparent words are clear, but religiously (diyanah) the divorce may not be effective according to some scholars. The issue of writing divorce under compulsion is also addressed: writing is a substitute for speech and is only valid when necessary; compulsion does not create necessity, so such a divorce is not valid. This shows that the rule for talaq has nuances depending on the mode of expression. The passage ends with the definition of talaq and the distinction between sarih and kinayah words, emphasizing that sarih words do not require intention, while kinayah words require intention for divorce to occur (though not for the judicial ruling in some cases?). The text stresses that for explicit words, even without intention, qada' holds it as talaq.

Key Terms
طلاق (talaq): Legally, the removal of the restraint of marriage immediately or eventually with a specific word.
عتاق (itq): Manumission; freeing a slave
مكره (mukrah): A person compelled to do an act under threat of harm
قضاء (qada'): Judicial ruling based on apparent evidence
دياية (diyanah): Inner religious reality; what is true before Allah regardless of apparent evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi ruling on talaq given by a person who is coerced (mukrah)?
A) The talaq does not occur because compulsion invalidates consent.
B) The talaq occurs because talaq is an act that cannot be annulled.
C) The talaq occurs only if the coercion is severe.
D) The talaq is suspended until the coercion ends.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that talaq and itq occur without intention and under compulsion because they are acts that cannot be annulled, with the exception of written divorce under compulsion.
